When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three kinds of cautery that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these some manner is that you make III cauteries, or IIII, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not hasten your hand to the whole cautery, and let the patient be supine on his back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II ners, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the heart which is opposite the mouse, or the cuts of the patient come from the left, and let the elevation by which you raise the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.  
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After it thrusts the two nerves inflamed until the hairs are pierced from the other side, and then draws out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see that, cauterize with the whole cautery to three nerves.  
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, except by the method called "asclytes."  
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit, then it is necessary that you make IIII cauteries around the head, and I on the stomach, and one on the liver, and I on the mice, and II behind the back on the spine, and I place the breast; and let the cauteries be near to the edge of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery open for long time to fight rot, and let not the care of the sick after the cautery; and healing would be hastened, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the clam that we have in front shows; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is here put before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrophic and are full of a yellow-white color, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply with it, thus tightly grasp the outer citrine, and let the cautery be according to this form: 
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do two legs two cauteries in each leg at the point of the cuvette; and let the cautery long, one below the knee front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open lengthwise without curing that it well be; after the cure of the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues that are in stomach and in intestine is flebbed, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the patient suffering well and of strong virtue, so do one great cautery on the stomach according to what he has spoken before or cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the subtle bud for every one cautery clavicle, and two cauteries on the loins.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are either at the base or one or more, and they are old and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then do cauteries: III above the spine of the back, that which is all outside below almecat pock and pock in triangulating, and I cautery below the bud II does; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face I do a large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the mice to all cauterize clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cure the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul", then heat the cautery which seems 1 razor, and then put it entirely inflamed on that "thelul" cut; and leave it as long as your hand until the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, because of which the blood is short; make this one or two times, and if there is much "thelul", you cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointment profitable as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, then comes such a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and it is filled and gives rottenness and corrupted moisture, then the wise man must carefully probe it with a probe, and keep that you know how long the probe is. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery which seems like a razor, and putting it in the fistula according to the quantity that the thing entered there, and re-start the cautery until the corrupted flesh be burned, once, or II or III, according to the quantity of need; and guard from burning the nerves which are in there, and the great veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, then guard these parts, and do not make those fuers except in their fleshy place, and think that she is not yet healed; after cure the place as long as it is healthy, and if the places are salved, and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the place is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is rotten, and corrupted the bones at the root; and thus like one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes as rains, and of great windiness, and does not take a husband, then it is necessary that you do cautery on the flanks on one side and the other with the cautery clavicle that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will give greater help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I do cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as our thumb; and I do one cautery outside the back, or two if you have need; and let the cautery clavicle be according to the form previously said.
de la marris	of the marsh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marsh is cold and moist, and does not allow for this to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one do them .iij. cauteries around the bud, as we have said of the cautery of the bladder, and .ij. cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be pointed, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found in the region of the viscus, therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip joint with .i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as that with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make three cauteries of the olive tree, large, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the others; and cure it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the bone of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of those things that we have said in the division and the cure is not good, and the illness is old: then it behooves you to purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to II manners: that is to say together medicines hot, and cautery of fire. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the bone of the hip III triangular cautery according to this form, and make good depth and great, and have between each cautery space the size of a finger, and let the cautery be olive; sometimes it is done cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, for which there are IIII according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a manner that the circles contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg.  
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and the cautery above the ankle four points, on the left side one point; and let the cautery be cuticular or burn the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, then cauterize where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "point." 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it be necessary, one does more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then one makes cautery with the cuticular or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so much that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do no more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left them until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.  
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of belly from which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner. 
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise said in the cautery of the hip, because this is how it is done, make I such iron and be at the head also large as a hazelnut or a little less, and be between the grooves and be from one groove to the other with space the quantity of a node of fist; and be the grooves on two parts, and be also like nuts, and let there be the hip of iron well made; and this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be it heated until it is all red and feel its heat, and then put it on the bone of the diseased hip, and let it be turned over to the healthy side; and cauterize once one cautery rent and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound covered for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and few see who uses it; and nonetheless those are good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burning is that you make the instrument in intertwining in which descends the edge of the gate, and be of iron or of steel a one appearance long, and in the height it has two, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a doe; and be opened outward and upwards, and join together according to this form:  
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After lay on the hip bone of the patient lying on his healthy side, and after your hand much on the hip bone; after cast between the two circles of the hot ash that be heated to fire I poc, and let it for an hour of time, and suffer the patient the heat and burn of it. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car it is found mordication also as of fire; and when the mordication is passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with a soft awe, and leave so III days, and put on butter until that which is black from the burn is ossified; and let him III days that rot in it; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, then you do the instrument that holds awry according to what you have done in the hip augment; and this is the manner of the hot awe, and I have written it or treated of the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening made by fire so that the point of a razor can enter; and puts one pot over the other well plugged, and puts on top alkali and heat and sweet wax, until there is the proper amount above the powders as you have well grasped it in your hand; and let it stay like this until it descends sweet water and pus or blood, then take all that, and throw it on the heat and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then if it will be much good and is administered in the work of medicine and cautery of other members Because it makes as well as fire works, and has other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip also like tessie and honey anacardi and charcoal with soap, all these things mixed together.  
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Gauls tell us a story of a cure in which a man was cured of pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and he praised it greatly, and said that no other treatment was given to him, and that he was healed at once when this treatment was done, and he bathed as he teaches afterward.  
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in this manner that you take dough of green litharge fresh and dry, and grind it well with a point of grease, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain holds, and the groin; and let it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burn.  
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into the bath as long as his body be a little aroused, and you make him enter into bed, and the pain will go away all and will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one must use cautery of such medicines unless after evacuation of the body. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fire from a sheep, it helps much; and it must be done with such manner of cautery. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and moisten it with old oil, and put it on the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called the fossa. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take pieces of dry goat, and put them on fire until they are coals, and place it on the wool, and let it stay until it is stained; and do again like this, and do not cease to do like this until you think by sense that it will come to the hip, and that the pain be ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by too much evacuation, or by similar appearance of spread cold matter, none of these appearances are worth cauteries, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be rid of fetid pills or other similar things that one makes on their back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with incise, and in each line 5 cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see it, make 3 or 4 cauteries at the clavical middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when they lie down, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine equally. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see so, cauterize around the spine with the burning cautery two lines or three, and let the points be near each other. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not apply a cautery in inflammation which is in the nerve's space. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints is from humors that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which they call properly “gout,” and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the hot cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the foot, then to it apply the cautery all over as one claims “point.” 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you do cautery on each knee III cauteries or IV of each side, with all the olive cautery; and if you need more, make more, but don’t hold your hand too hard except as long as the tip of the heart is burnt. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, so make points around the fossa II lines; and if there remains no pain in the two sides, so make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, so cauterize each part, and make good governance to the patient and penre medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the groin, and the testicles descend to the hips and it is new, then when you see it cured, let him not urinate that day; and let him use things which lift the belly, so that the cord descends from his belly; after, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his leg as long as the testicles are repaired, and move them to your thighs, and direct the incision below the rupture upon the bone of the hip, and a sign that is similar to half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until it is white and it feels soft. 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return back; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other one on the hip which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign to all your hand, and hold it straight and as far as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, begin again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful that the bone does not jump when you do the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or other harm. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your works are worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of large people also large according to their measure; after III days cure their wound with butter until the burning is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie for XL days on his back until the wound is well joined; and it is necessary that his dressings be long so that the boils do not come out when he wants to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he will want to rise, administer to him a good splint, and bear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he work little and guard himself from too much repletion of drinking and eating, and from too great lifting; and when he follows these teachings so is he completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here afterwards the cure of tailoring in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come into other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then to them do I apply the cautery of the fire according to its quantity, and be it burned at the third part of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one must cauterize with the cautery of three angles according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the place of the incision and make a line across the breadth above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand in all the cautery clavicle. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and milder. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or from being struck, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "point," and let the cauterization be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and turns and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, because it is customary that it must change in the member to which it is nearest, for which reason you should make the cauteries as long as the patient is healing.  
de meselerie	of treachery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are aided at times by cautery with great help, and even the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see the one to be cauterized, take care that the patient is at the beginning, and if she is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not send or remain, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the sick person, then you make V cautery on his head: I put the head at nine, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and II on the II horns, and I behind on the nape; and keep your hand so that the cauteries come to the bone, and as long as the crusts go out so that the vapors of the large humors can issue; and cauterize on the face according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mesentery is spread everywhere; and it appears clearly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and 1 cautery on its neck, and 2 cauteries on the spine of the collar, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and 1 large one on the hip and 1 other on the side, and 2 on the 2 shoulders; and 2 on the knees, and 2 on the tendons of the thigh, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard yourself from the nerves that are on the last calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cautery on the bone of the forearm, and 1 other on the bone of the stomach, and 1 other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when more fire cautery is done, the more it helps, and it profits; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already all corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in ways of irons.  
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure of the place with flour of veils with honey and other cures until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not cured, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with dressings until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at times cautery is done by hand and by foot and on the back, at the place where the nerve that numbs the limb exits, and thus in this way the swelling is removed; and nevertheless let no one interfere unless he knows the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body. 
de albaras	of breeches
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease which is called "albaras" is present, and the means of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize with a cautery a point through and through, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the blemished part is removed, and its color changed; then cure with flour of rice and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondras, of each one part; and let everything be mixed together, and let it be bound with a cloth, and let it air at the site until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a boil by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When an ulcer comes at the beginning, and you see it to be arrested, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the sages say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the sore; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen many times; and more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circule," as we have said in much about cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes time to die or because of the superfluity that it produces or because of the blood of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the heat; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that leave it as it is.  
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced throughout with the cautery, then heat the cautery of this which is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rotteness is allayed.  
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness there is which is called “corroding”, and it is nothing other than a consumption of a limb, because it eats away the limbs as if the fire were consuming dry branches. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can endure fire cautery, then sharpen the small and large cauteries carefully, according to what is necessary for the place where the illness is; after that, cauterize all parts as much as you reach all corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted be removed.  
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for III days, and put on the cauterized places softened gruel with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of engendering flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after III days that the wound is healthy and not growing, it's good; and if it isn't, begin again the cautery on those parts which are remaining corrupted. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this wound has sometimes been cured with the medicine of fire in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicine of fire in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the spurs that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that in the feet by fire is born a malady which is called "clubfoot" according to our understanding, and it is a great thing that cripples the foot. 
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to II manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and cautery of hot water. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron cautery as well as it is a feather of wool, and it be made of good iron to the measure that it can turn around the nail on all sides, and that there have subtle edges; after this put all hot over the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and let it thus for III days until it begins to fester; then I make a plaster of wild mallows ground with seil, and let the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots.  
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place with ointment, preventing pus until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and often happen in hands and feet, then you must bring them cautery of hot water; and it is in this manner: take a cane of iron or iron, or a pen of vulture, and put on the nail and the handle, that is to say spurs warts; and put the cane on so that it pricks all around, then I put a drop of hot water, and hold well your hand, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water path deep until the root; and suffer the patient a little the burning of hot water an hour; then let him as is, and it will be rooted out all its roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another until you have searched all those who are on the body, then cure the openings that produce flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or from quartan fever or other, it is fitting that you make to him .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each spine; and .i. cautery or pez, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; so let him stop trembling, and hasten the healths from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At no time appear by fire the body baths, or pus pimples, that come from large corrupt matters. 
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at the beginning when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: a fine cautery of myrtle wood, so that its tip be seized by fire, or of long arisologe root, or of the lentil-shaped cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes the cauterize is done at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from them forward, but are disrupted the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great hemorrhages occur from the artery that is cut at the wound which comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to extend.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, hasten to place your two index fingers upon the wound of the vein and restrain it strongly until the blood is quieted under your two fingers, and no drop issues forth more; then put to fire the olive cauteries smaller and larger as many as they are all red; then grasp one, or a large or small one according to the wound and its place where the artery is cut, and place the cautery upon that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps forth when you lift your fingers from upon the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to make these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when a vein shrinks from the artery, it cannot be well tightened even when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying with thread, or by medicines placed upon which have power to tighten the vein; and be bound and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring a tightening of the ligature or tight bandaging or placing burning things upon it, or similar things, if it does not profit so much.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to any and he has no medicine present, then he must put his two fingers upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and tightly bind it until it is tightened above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but often moisten it with cold water that be very cold until the vein is congealed and thickened and tightened; and make then those things which he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all illness in which it is necessary cautery of fire, or burning medicine, and incisions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I put that chapter from the head just to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those one finds more easily those one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.  
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come to cures. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have been afflicted so with their sickness that they die easily because of the treatment they find for their illness, and because of the greatness of their evil; and of these one must have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give their meaning to you and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the patient is deceitful.  
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It does not behoove you that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have gained and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and memory of length. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter to you by chapters, according to those that are before, the chapter of cauteries, which I have told you from the head to the feet, for those that you find more easily those that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the birth is strained too hard the child's head; and some time it comes from a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and in all that I have seen it hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the treatment  in these ways.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not support it; and they thought so much moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled below the bone under the scalp, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such as if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut in the head a wide fissure; and it be as long as two fingers, as far as the moisture goes; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, do two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the sutures of the head open from each part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you; then it is necessary that you cut in the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision remove the moisture all outside.  
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After having strained the incisions of cloth and powders, and put wine and oil in there, and leave it so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with tents and ointments, and let the chief bandage be strapped, and then give the patient dry meat from the source of moisture as long as the limb is fortified and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where appears the greatness of the abscess, and its assembly of liquid; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, cut where the abscess appears, and its filling of liquid, and make it according to what you have power over it; and guard that you do not cut the artery; and vein flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the decrease of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of summary
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease which is called 'catarrh' in the eyes or at the breast, and the sickness is old, and the medicine cure profits not at all, then the last cure is the cautery with these one copes the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you see them covered, that the patient raise his head; afterwards rub their neck with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck with all the cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are after the ears, and so they are put back; then mark the veins of inche, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula from part II, until the tail comes to the bone, and this must be by the wide side of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting also as .ij. fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood leaps out from above continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of III finger widths, then make an incision and cut up to the bone; and as much as it is necessary to put out blood is VI c., and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point without syphilis, then let it be covered that pus does not come, then strain the wound and tie it, and the care of ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moistures of tears and the heats in the temples and ancient sores and similar things, and it is medicated by manners of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit them, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes back the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not easily replaced except in some men who are too cold; and if it is replaced, he strains the neck of the patient with some drapery, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above the pinches, and depart well of the threads that are under each side; and if the artery is subtle, then turn it to the point of the needle, then cut from that part according to the quantity of the two joints. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not jump without pain throughout. 
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from six ounces, up to three; and if the artery is large, it behooves you to tie it in two lengths of a strong double thread of silk, so that rot may not come before the healing of the wound, and there be excessive bleeding; then cut off the superfluity which is between the two ligatures at the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize with the cuticular cautery up to the bone until the chills are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and he is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is aid to finish the moistures: for this reason it is of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill their place with old cotton and put on tents well made; and when they are undone, may be cured with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a bit of the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place with vitriol and strain your hand that the wound be staunch; and if you do not have those things present, put on the place your finger until the wound is congealed, and raise the place of cold water until the bleeding stops, and it be strained as much as it is required; and what is more helpful and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery trenching of .ij. parts, but the trenchings be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thick, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one of a good width, and then when you have marked the two parts with your knife, and you place the red-hot iron on it until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two fingers; and be kept apart the two arms because it is not well joined by this cautery at all; and that is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow down the veins that are on the forehead of the head of fire, and it does not profit medicine treatment when it is done, and you see the face of the sick person wrinkle, and feel on his forehead ambulation as if from tremors; and where the eye is wet and moist so that the hair of the eyelids falls out, and the eyelids are dried up, and burned by the heat of tears, such a cure is necessary.
