Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the ancients "cure contused," and is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he may have or forehead, then make III cuts or forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts as II should all remove the forehead down to neif, and the other II as II ribs above the papers, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries that are as II ribs above the papers; and move your hand away from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of III does across joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the sharp spatula of II parts of which this is the form:  
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is under the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the .ij. incisions to tot lou syfac which is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract further this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if it is put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellaire," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the rib cutting toward the air side of the heart, and the rib root toward the bone, and the butt until it comes to the middle cleft.  
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as the eyes until the incision is continuous to that which opens the heart, and then another part do in the middle of the fissure until the other side; and then withdraw the blood equally, and express their place for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and asafoetida, and keep that abscesses no come; and on the third day untie the linen, and there administer great plantlets of tepid water, then the cure of ointment basil with rose oil, and other cures which one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any one comes an acute catarrh, and you see the eyes red and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where the head is affected by a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure that is there, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to retract his forehead, then make a great cut between the brow, and another double Ipoc. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begins from the split of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the meal; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sever between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandage; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, that make flesh begin. 
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it on these wounds to dry up the char completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone or similar thing as iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing thing such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then set the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if there is distilled any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with condiment, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and raise the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes force by this cure; and if it does not come force, then administer the extraction with subtle pincers, for this is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with the fine single-edged tool; and if it does not come out by this, make a wire loop and insert the head of the loop or through the opening of the ear forcefully, and stop what is around the loop with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter with the loop; then pull it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take a bit of wool which is used to catch birds, and put it on any instrument which is pointed for doing this, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the wool onto the stone or whatever thing it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear so that an abscess comes out, and spasms; and the manner of the cutting is that you first bleed the patient of the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer i. spathule tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case therefore that water falls into the ear it is necessary for the patient to use externally of condiments first, and plug the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lying on that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaped for this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it is not so, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; and put them in the patient's ear where it is perforated, and raise it with their foot from the other side, and place another stone on the one which is in the ear; and cease not to do this of stone into stone until the water flows completely, and thus she will come out completely; and if you see, then take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and the other end grip it with fire until the reed is burnt as much as possible; then redo the other part of the reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, then administer extraction of pincers; and this is the thing easier to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it is fitting that you look at the ear in the sun: if you see no worms, then treat them with subtle pincers; and if they do not appear, then take the cane of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And thrust the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed in forming all the chain; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to be moved, so stop the ear with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treating distillations; and if distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, from which this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be of silver or iron, it is narrowed below to 1 small openings, and above open for distilling; and for pressing within the distillation 1 instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take 1 razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines in the chain, and the chain be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and the feeling of the patient within, and let the distillations be 1 pock heated over the fire so as when it is distilled in the ear; and keep that it be not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by means of a wound, or a piece of flesh born inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes come from within the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes they happen .i. poc (one) by force and the hole is seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from within so that it cannot be seen, is of grievous harm in many cases, and in this, you should place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the hair appearing, then the work has taken its full course, for this is how it is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be careful and cut in front and behind all the way through, so that it does not blister the ear; if the hair is from flesh born or a piece of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers and cut it lightly, until all of the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is made in the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it a little in the fire, then put it into the body of the ear.  
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce it lightly, and make sure that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment which comes on sheets of paper from the eyes when they are moist and are dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut it with a spatula from its roots; then put on top vitriol ground.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it being cut out, you cauterize with a subtle lentil-shaped cautery, and the cauterization after the incision heals well; and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the sprain
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers of the eyes things that seem cracked in its shape and in its hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of moisture large in the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hail moves from one part and another, and this is a light thing to know; then make the large opening, then the skin of each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a bit of the paper, do not bother the patient; and if the tear is large, stitch it together and care for it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, because the flesh will restore itself quickly and generate tissue.  
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the inside of the ear toward the top, so reverse the paper, and being the hail to tweezers, and the cut and pressed on both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not harm; and when the hail is cut, let the eye of salt water, and cure the place of that which hinders flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is engendered in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and grieves them much at their eyes, and it comes to them the catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces down, and sleep on it, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two and feel the extirnation between.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your breast; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then put it on him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a pointed spatula, a fissure of a width, and not be more than the wound one makes in the vein; and make the skin cut to the bottom until you come to the exinach; and in more cases comes exinach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract therefore with all one piece of cloth charpit between your fingers on the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, until you come to the whole spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the skin does not open at the beginning of the incision, then carefully widen the incision slightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in wine and water, and put them on top, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind seed and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which is stagnant. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure as long as he is sound. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, so its cure with plasters soothing until it is healed.  
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs grow crooked other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and bring many diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, so much that it is because of the destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. ways: either by cautery together with fire, or by medicine ague according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then insert a needle to .i. thread above; and let this be below the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow near these hairs, and draw .i. thread up to all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the crooked hairs, to all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and drapeil, then place on top of the paper a figure of enche, such as the myrtle leaf, and anyway it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is devised to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is someone who needs it, one cuts a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is soft; then makes on the whole spatula on the II lines that you have signed, and begins of lou great tear up to small; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the width of a root, then puts the pincers in one of the II angles of the heart, then scrapes all; then assemble the II lips at a seam of a needle with all I fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of the threads on the II eyebrows to any sticky things, if you want to do this; and if not, have no care, then leave the suture and the threads until III days or IIII; then cure the wound without suture with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the soldering of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is moved (as the ancients say), and this work without fear; and if in another manner: and that you sign the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, to III pincers unlatched according to the form that is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what surpasses the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle that has thread, and put it in the figure; and put the other thread by the great tear, and the second thread by the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said of the incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the thorns is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij. thorns by art, and .ij. subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut off the two heads from two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly on top of the paper above the eye, and restrain the .ij. thorns of the .ij. parts that form; and let it so for some days, and the leather which is restrained will die and wrinkle and carry, as long as it dries by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the cauterizes with some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is joined, and if it has lifted the paper, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the II canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you prick a fine needle, and put one thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the shoulders and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and tie the chief of the threads; then put the patient's head on your healthy one; and be under the sun so that the work is clarified, because it is a subtle and small work; then put the needle all the way to the chase into the root of the hair joint, and make it pierce the paper hastily as long as you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put into the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the hairs come out all the way to the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then draw the chase downwards to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair is hardened in its place and the flesh grows up; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair with the natural ones, and raise it with that one or leave it, as long as it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness which is called « aleacrati » or rot comes in the eye, there are two ways of it: one natural and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden blow of wound, or cutting or cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the operation on it is that you cut that joint and open its lips, and put linen tents inside, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not necessary that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Because if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but there is work of softening things, such as fennel; and the rose of water or althea and flaxseed are cooked, and diachylon ointment melted in any oil, and it envelops a tent, and the cure from this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before; and these operations that we have said are nothing but remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is dislocated is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and splits and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an needle, in which it has double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread goes into the two shoulders of the flesh; then place the flesh above the whole needle, and the cut with the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the parchment returns according to what is right, it is good; if those no, then take the razor and place it in the fissure, and turn the parchment, and make fissures where it costs inside the parchment; and be the heads of the two fissures at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and be made angles so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no «I greche»; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs are raised below, of those who follow the parchment, then adjust the two parts separated, and sew them with a thread of wool; then care for those that we have said about softening medicines, and poultices, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a tear or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is above; then sew between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip anything of all their power how they make return the figure to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sewing of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to a human hand in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor do its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the being as pincers, until you cut what is attached to the spatula, which should be neither too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too thick does not wound the eye; and let your incision, by which you remove that assembly, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all of that assembly, and do no times in the salty water of the eye, and the lift of fresh water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in egg white; and after the third day use collyrium and things soft until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in .ii. manners: it is nervous and similar to .i. hard syfac, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and one cooks it panre as pincers, it cannot do; and one and the other semblance begins towards the great tear duct, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head in your hand, then they open their eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pincers with small curvature, and bring it upwards; then take a needle, and put .i. hair of horse, or boar, or ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a poc and insert it into the angle, and pierce it all the way through the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and bring it upwards, and scrape along the entire edge of the angle following the curve and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining part in the root of the tear duct all around with the subtle spatula and as small forces, and leave the natural char or tear duct, so that by incision the body of tears does not come accustomed; and no times extend the angle alone, and to the thread, as we have said; then scrape on the entire spatula below of which is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision, put in the eye a bit of ground silk, and of the collar made of lead, and let it stay until the next day; then cure it as much as it needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, do the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail slightly, and if you see that it does not decrease and the reasoning accelerates, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of lead and red collar and ground silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, as long as it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil abscess, then milk it, and treat the boil first until it is healthy, then resume the work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it at the corner, and cut a part and not half altogether, that no body of tears comes out; then distill in the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red and cover the pupil and restraint upon the eyelids and turn to the fire, and seems like a rose of battle; and the work so is that the patient puts his head in your healthy one, then the works the eyes, and coil all that flesh with needles suitable to them, and sustain him at the force; then chop the first flesh, and go all chopping to the razor until the end, and keep that you do not blind the eye in the work; and be the incision of the spatula which we have said in the incision of the angle and as little forces of which one takes away the pupil, as the form after this chapter demonstrates it; and when the incision is accomplished and taken away all the flesh, so employ the oil of silk broiled or you distill red pepper and seeming medicines corrosive, and put on the eye fire with cotton with a bit of egg white, so that it may be assured of a hot abscess; and if he remains nothing there, and the cold blood surrounds him, and you doubt a hot abscess, so leave the eye and cure the abscess of things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work as long as it is healed, and thus do as many flesh are adjusted in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you align the cure of each weak oil of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red that are covered over the eye, and they take away from the sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary for the first that you look at the eye, in what state it is, and if there is no other disease besides the cataract; therefore, coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy one, then suspend those veins throughout the whole body according to your wisdom, and be the tendons subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two threads be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, with this coil, as forcibly suspend those veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see removing those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and make this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, then instill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrode what remains of the red vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all these in that hour, make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it lie for some days until the pain is calmed and the abscess is assured hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire are called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it by cautery and by medicine burning hot according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you open on the abscess, where it must die, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the king has all the instruments of what is here the form; and it is called "sharp chief", and is made of fire iron to one chief reont, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is reset; and do this several times, then return to the place of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is sutured, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is sutured, and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is not suppurating, know that it is healthy; if not, there is no other means than to bring back the fistula to the opening according to this form: And it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take I the forest according to this form, and let the shoulder be of iron at three angles, and the fist be attenuated up to the head as you see here. 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye a little, then turn to all the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this, if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the place, then the matter goes to the cheek; thus it is lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye's issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open throughout and there is no disturbance in the cheek, or lessening, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal, then place suction cups or a hat on them without injuring to suck, then put on the eye i. one layer made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then restrain the eye, and plaster it over with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each one in 4, and then put one above the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then strain it from above with a stiff bandage form, and recommence suction cups to suck without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the plasters soften, then it is necessary that you strain them very much; then remove the plaster after a day and a night, and if you see the eye repairing, it's good; if not; then begin again the plastering and the bandages and the plasters and the suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	about the dislocation of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and it comes forth from the papers like i. grain of resins, and it is explicable to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle in the root of the part below until the one above, then put another needle where there is i. double thread of the part of the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the end of the double thread and tie a part of the weave together, and restrain it well, then remove the needle and put on the eye with half an egg white; and let it stay until the threads are joined with the weave, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the weave on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter then immediately; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the pouch of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called «alcunnati» is nothing other than a bow which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a properly prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the bow coming upward to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and do not let it descend and let the light be scattered, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bow is issued; and when it is issued, distill in the hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then be cured of another cure until it is healed.  
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have done the similar things of the daggers in division, and those which are fitting for examination; if in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie his good eye and hold it very tight; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if his eyes are left, or in your right hand if his eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if his eyes is left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if his eyes is right; then put the point of the instrument beside the cornea by the thickness of a straw in that white part of the eye to the part of the least tear, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" virtuously, and withdraw your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is at the parfont of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackening; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal fabric, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then express it under one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water descends now, if the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.  
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little, and if the liquid rises up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ensconced and it does not rise up, gently extract the almagda by turning your hand back and forth; then put back in water a little bit of seil gemme, and leave from this the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of fire on the eye plugged with wool or linen soaked in rose oil and honey, and bind it with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top common flour with abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deep in it, but make it subtle then put almagda, as we have said; and at the accomplishment of the work equip the patient with the bed approaching, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition up to the third day; then untie it in the same darkened room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back until the seventh day; and it is not proper that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this, for that reason that the water ascends quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, you shall loosen the eye before the seventh day, and apply the thing that calms the abscess; and when it is appeased, then unbind the view and put on its face a border to cover for any day, and let it be in that dark place.  
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he leaves the house step by step, and converts himself to his case; and know that none of disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almagd pierced, so that one sucks the water, but anyway I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them see them; and be of the grain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of the same subtlety, and the last in three angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nerve
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At no time are there born or generated various joined limbs, so that there are some who seem scorpions with many feet; and if there are such ones where it has flesh of wicked color, and if it has flesh of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these ears which is souef, and not enchancree, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and put the one ear in those ears, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the ear is entirely removed.  
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that one cannot cover, open it to all i.e. the instruments subtle and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without tear or abscess, then secure it as is proper; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and are removed all the humors, then giete or wine or water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut; therefore it behooves you to put a piece of linen thread into it, about as thick as possible, and be coated with hands us, and have between each knot a space of I must or less; and put the patient's shoulder on the thread in his nostril at its power, and pull it gently until it comes out of the nostril into the mouth; and many times do children thus in school, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do so; then hold the head that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart from each other, carefully observing those which are or threads. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back in place as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the head a plaster of lint for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills the oils and medicines in the head: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a basin, and lead it thus; and if you see fit, make a closed basin, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the top for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nerve
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
