Many times upon the nerve of the head a disease arises called "telul," and grows and becomes large indeed, until it is a terrible thing to behold; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all of it, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, be warned, if it is hard, of dark color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron for it is an inflamed abscess, because when you cut it any time, much evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not dark in color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with drying things and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nerve is cut and covered
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these working cartilages, it does little good, for in some men.  
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, if it is seen that the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips together with a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder over powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put over the powders a piece of plasters of strong or other melting plaster, and leave it until it drains by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitch is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths, abscesses hard like grains of corn appear, some smaller and some larger; therefore you should turn the lips and cut above each one with a knife, take it with forceps and cut it in each part; then put vitriol powder on the incision site until the blood is stopped; and then apply a salve, and care for the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum's flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore you should hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, and let the wound bleed; then put vitriol powder or other astringent and drying powders on the site; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens often, cut it a second time and cauterize it; if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the chief of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, sores that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and greenish, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are smelly; so it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws in your saint, and pull out the teeth or the scabs appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do of the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other stains, as long as they are worldy; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, then it begins again on the second day and the third, until you have all pulled; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to pull, according to what the work shows them, because the scraper with which one pulls out the outer teeth has other forms than those with which one pulls between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It behooves when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to draw as much blood as possible, because one should not do it poorly; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure treatment, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain troubles the patient, and thinks that it is a tooth of Saint, and makes milk the good tooth; and all the way does not depart the pain because of this, as long as the evil remains, for we have already wanted to do it to these patients; and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a sharp spatula strong to guard the gums on all sides; then move it to your fingers or with tweezers at the first bit and bit, as long as it is well loosened, then affirm well the tweezers; and let the head of the patient be in your saint between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is pulled straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and put it gently inside each side, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, it is necessary that you fill it with bandages, where the holes are; and if you restrain it carefully with pliers, that it does not break when restraining it; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.  
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore take good care that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient through the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like ignorant healers who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the bone and bring no cure as we have said; but often come with great sickness because of the roots that remain or from the bone they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, apply vitriol powder to it; and if that does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must first make teeth, are at long points and with large handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be of well-made iron, and be toothed to hold securely.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, then you must put on it moist cotton in butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are open, put in the pliers called "algefri," so that the head appears like a beak of a bird; and be made inside like a file, and this is the form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because of this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, it is good; if these do not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two prongs, of which is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are in front in the fashion of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large pliers, of which is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break a bone or of the other bones, or he can, then search for the instruments that it is needed, that I have told you, and help with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in chaste women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot smooth it nor file it; therefore the ridge; and if it is joined with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to .i. small beak, and be of sharp iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping is little by little in the hands for a few days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then the file of a piece like this is the shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in a few days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plain at the end to all without a razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it to move it without it falling out, and you have treated it with constricting medicines, and this does not work; if so, it is necessary to restrict it with a gold wire, because the silver wire turns green and corrodes, but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are close together, take the wire and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth between the healthy teeth, if there is one or more, until you come sagely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start the covering again up to the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and sagely, until it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grip the bone fragments with tongs, and assemble them, and place them between the sound teeth, and set it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it tightened as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the wires break, restrain it with another wire; let it remain like this and will serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the setting of the II sound teeth, and the II broken ones, just as you see. 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; and let no one intervene who is not wise and patient, and at some time the form of a tooth made of bone from a hoof is made, and it is placed in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restrained as we have said, and it remains and serves this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament that comes from under the tongue or by nature, is born thus; or by accident of a suture wound; and the work is such that you work the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament broad, until the tongue is dislocated from its place; and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from a suture wound, then put the probe and cut broadly that ligament; and guard that the cutting be not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, lift the level of rose water and oil, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and tie the patient every night, that the ligaments may not solder.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows, put powdered vitriol on the spot; and if the bleeding doesn't stop, cauterize it with a leaden cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, so put the awl, and make it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding persists in your work, so put on vitriol ground until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you draw all out; then lift the place with warm water and cold, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come from within the throat growths that are called “godath,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is abscesses hard of little sense and with fusse color, do not touch them with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid blood loss; but let it stay until it is dead, and then you will split it, where it would break by itself; and if it is of white color, and the root is subtle, have the instrument prepared to cover, but first see if the abscess heats up and calms. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his knees be in your health, and he opens the mouth and the surgeon places the forceps between his hands, and presses the tongue down with all the instrument, from this is the form; and be it of silver or fine iron as well as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the pincers and put them in the almond, and pull up with force as much as you can; and do nothing of these things with the cloths, then cut with the instrument, this is how it is done, that seems like forces; and nonetheless the chief are bent, one place against another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, cut with pliers, this is how it is done:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side, and the other side not; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and vinegar, and if a discharge of blood occurs, gargle the patient with water, or the peels of pomegranates are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stanched; then treat it until it is healed; and no time others abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them like the two almonds as well.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say the abscess of small size; and I had well closed all the throat so that the woman could not expire through the passage which was stopped, and could neither eat nor drink, and would be dead if she remained thus one day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so raised that it had been put II fingers by the II openings of the eyes.  
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had therefore, and placed one in the mouth, then I pulled out the throat, and into a large portion of gut; then I put another part in the other side of the two, and I opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I put the instrument in these abscesses, and in coped a part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus was unstopped the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I tightened it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I left these parts, and know only that God did with her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the grape is at its fullest and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is of less size and round, it is called "grape". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the head of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it is necessary that you evacuate the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.  
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously; then insert the pin into the eye, and pull it downwards, and the cup to the one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of the cutting, it is necessary that you use an instrument for the cauterization of the senses fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp point. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy side, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with a live water sock, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the end of this instrument, of this it is the form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have or head a hair that one puts the medicine in, as like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine on top of the grape; and let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle will come from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the larynx; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it burning and the medications of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the chain above, until the cotton dries on the grape; and do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and leave it after four or five days. And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, then begin it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, of cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysop and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in 1 pot, and put it inside, and make it boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have 1 instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or of iron, and be the one of the shoulders put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the eye by the vein, until the eye is mortified; after that he begins again, until the eye dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for more things happen there; and do not make this except at the declination of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put inside its head a piece of wood, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; because the piece of wood does not make the vapor aggravate the mouth, and it is good cure altogether health. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine gets lodged in the throat, or some other thing; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue in the sun with all your instrument, so that you see the thing move; and that which does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit, as long as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will bring forth the thing by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or 1 morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge 1 thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge itself, and then you draw forth; and if it does not come forth by those things which we have said, then take 1 instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come loose, nor push in the bone; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he will know whether or not the thing is difficult; if he pushes down, or he draws it forth equally throughout the entire instrument, until it is forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is medicine given to the insane, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when these do not help, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the hemorrhage, then treat it with all small forceps or subtle pliers that are suitable for this.  
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a dog’s hair, and put it into the throat of the sick person, then put where the end of the hair is hot iron, and do this often.  
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient remains thirsty all day.  
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full cup of cold water, and work the mouth, and put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he falls. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will yield without hurting. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is this that you take a pot where it has charcoal, and let it be covered with a coverlet pierced in the middle, and in that one pierce the head of the instrument; then put your fumigation, and the patient puts his head of the pipe in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not go out, but comes to the nostril; and the nostril will now run, and if it does not run, then recommence the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then the matter is necessary that it should be expelled by this government. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the sinuses, is, when one can see it, similar to tongs curved so as to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness from lime, so that what it takes, it cannot leave behind; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to what remembrance comes after this in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in II ways one of which is in its own resemblance, and of those that hold moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is other than those that come in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce until the bowel is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if to some such that it is necessary to pierce when they are crusty, and do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and it is left as long as it is rotting, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; where it is near the base, pierce it as soon as it is ripe; and it is not proper that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for the one which is near the base, so that it does not go too deep, and becomes lengthened inside, and a fistula comes; and cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the separation of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and of the suppuration and the softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more depends the location of the abscess, and where it appears to bulge; and be the perforation long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these which are broken, according to that limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before those, the body of the venom will be lengthened from him, and it is full of much filth; and by chance it hardens the lips and the depths of it. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are perceived according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb needs.  
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to sever the core, and cover; when it has become as a drapery, and is withered, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such that one cuts like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the branches; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times little by little, until the pus is all gone; same if the patient is of weak strength, or pregnant woman, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit often twists with the issue of the bowels, which by chance may kill the patient, and you do not worry about it. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if you wipe the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, then administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it inside, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint shavings without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then the osteotomy, and cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, so administer cold water and easily, and wet the cloth, and put it on the bleeding place many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is during winter, and the places or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths moistened with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then undo the abscess and wipe it and care for it, as is fitting, until it is healed.  
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses: I have said to you how one should proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of suppurations
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where heart of the head come small abscesses, and are mannered of us that are in webs, as well as the joint of a bird's wing, and much in resemblance. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and like such that have moisture as well as pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony in the waist, and there is no doubt that if the artery does not do otherwise. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are such that you should probe with all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," from which its form comes after, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then raise it by means of a long one. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, then scrape it without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns quickly if we leave it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and wine, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are still remaining dry. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of any pain; then cure the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in fat, then cut it according to this form, long; and put your tweezers there, and scrape it on all sides, and put all your care of drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is festering, and of the size and of the cure as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the tail on a pus-filled abscess and moist one is easier, because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and among those abscesses that I examined on a very old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had made an incision in it, one would have done just as well as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, for that which come at the chief of children and at the roots of ears, the opening shall be always to the most dependent place, so that it may bring out the pus; and the cure as it is fitting. 
des scrophules	of scrofulous sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come from other parts or body, and are bad, and are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its side, like the boil and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and if there are malicious ones who do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that therefore you see of good disposition in the skin, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not hard to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it above, and the peel from each part, and are the two lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and apply it piece by piece, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be too sharp nor trenching, so that the hand does not escape, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound ground vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and strain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it; then examine with your index finger if there remain any small pustules, if so cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrofula a vein large, it does not become that you cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and leave it to hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cover. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all of the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no delay of superfluity for the size of the scrofula.  
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk out, and the count as we have said.  
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulous ulcers that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; and pierce thus as the one said before, depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure with ointment inciting flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the throat opening called "epiglottis" be cut; and one does not help them by this, because all the veins and arteries of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in .ij. almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV a small incision through, between the II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no meat, and the vessels are long from this. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it behooves him to stretch the skin of the throat to all the neck, then split the cartilage until it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the epiglottis, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the mucus of the windpipe that is flowing from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed of which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound at the heart, and close all alone with sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim said one does not do this juice until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to death, and the defect the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, close the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe and they breathe through the wound, and so they are saved from death; and for this reason, the elders commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is passed, and it is passed in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to heal her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that came from it, and so well that it had not pierced a vein nor been led except through the throat, and the veins were driven out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it, and thus I dressed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the girl except that she lost her voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a wound, and it is mostly in women; and it is according to two ways: natural, and accidental; where the natural has no instrument. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to grease for us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work to make outside than in this which is small, and the prove and search throughout the introducer: if you find it as I grease, and cannot at any vein, so chop it, as one chops the ours, and the train to all its head, if there is no point; and surround well everything, and cure it as it behoves, until it be perfectly healthy. 
des nous	Of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many manners are to us, of which I will say all the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between ours and the outcome.  
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling is not passed, and the rot is complete; therefore rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains I the abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as well as a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two resemblances, or greasy, or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division.  
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the new one, that you feel and inquire first of all the instrument which is called "entromisoiro," according to its form that will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses for us is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, and take care of what may jump out.  
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture is running short, whatever color it has, treat it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the introduction there comes no more moisture, know that it is fatty, therefore treat it in a cross, and take it with forceps, and gently scrape each side and ward the coat where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the point; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out piecemeal so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve, apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and restrain the wound, and put on top soothing things an abscess hot, and cure of other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is great, it binds the two lips of the wound, and cures of those who engender flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein being cut is contrary or otherwise you hurry and apply the place of vitriol ground, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound purges, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cover what remains from the outside.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the intrumentary instruments, and are of III manners: great and medium and small; and there are III squares that are called "albaret," and I which is called "breb," and there are of III manners: great, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistula; and are also like the needles with which one sews the spells, and are of citrine iron, or silver, and most valuable those that are yellow, and are more proven by black pitch to enclose the borders of fistula; and are of III manners: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are probes that have two curves in three ways also; and there are probes that have three curves, and are also in three ways; and there are probes that have two curves, and probes of one curve only, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these things are sharp tools, and there are some which do not cut more than one side, with which we peel the skin. Because of this, one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and of these instruments, the lancets are put in handles so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three manners: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy places like legs, arms, breasts, and around the genitals, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling peels of fists, according to this form, with which one drains blood.  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put at times in the place which heals by cutting of veins, and arteries, and at times are reopened according to this great form
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they appear like the breasts of women; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them should follow this form from this line b to line g:  
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound, preventing it from growing, then assemble the two sides of the wound by sewing, and treat it until it is healed; if it leans down and is softened as often happens with women, make it in two ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two sides, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or if the incision is not quite made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of blood loss, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining part and the fat, then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous sores or boils, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
