Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply to the wound old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment from that point on until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a boil, treat it like we said in the section on cutting boils, and if the wound goes back into a pocket of pus, apply a cautery like we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the artery's rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is routed and the skin is sewn that is above, there often comes abscesses, and it also happens to the vein inflamed and abscess; and if the one knows thus when it is for the artery, then the abscess is long in being made; and when you feel it at your fingertips, then you feel its tightening; and when this is for the vein, then it is red outwards appearing; and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and arms and neck and in many other places, and is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It behooves therefore to shun the cure of iron, and he who is at chief behooves also to shun it, and in him who is swelling of artery making by above the skin of the long; then works the size as quickly, and departs well the artery from the webs, as long as she is discovered; then put under it a needle, and let her pierce up to the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place which is between the II links of an introducer as long as the pus which is there, and be healed the abscess; then administer the cure that enjarne bowe, as long as the thread hangs; then cure those of ointment coming after these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, so you must hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and let her pierce, and there have the double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or link of one of II parts as II chiefs of thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issuing, so put another needle to all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in IIII lengths; then cut the abscess as long as the superfluities issue, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put on I drapeil moilliet in wine and oil, then administer cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.  
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are injured, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often as shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and it is I grief abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain; and when one restricts it forcibly, the patient feels pain, and is not fully in conformity with the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go contraction; and the one that is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin to spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on a hook, and scarify it, then drain it and stitch up the wound and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large mouths hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes they happen in the belly and not somewhere else thetulous, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of the semblance of them, and are the roots subtle, and the head large; and there are small and very large; and I saw the man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine root, and they were split, and flowed moist.   
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you look at if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root; if the cope to the spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist often comes too great bleeding, and if the blood does not stop, then hurry to cauterize it; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a thread of lead well made, and bind the limb as we have said, and leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the lead thread until it cuts the limb, and dries by itself without work; and if the roots are large, you have fear to cut completely even for the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful that you do not cut the tendon which is of pale color and poor feeling and milk-white. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has burst open, and I will come to the treatment of this boil after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the head is healed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the breasts, as they happen in other ruptures, or of blood that spills from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and by the issue of the pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from diverse exit. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides it rises up, and then returns, and perhaps it is tightened, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for strong work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses are thick and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is swollen on touching, and the works are that you see if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So it befits you to leave the care. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For he has doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.  
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then it is necessary that you command the patient to hold his arm, and be extended straight, then seize all around the belly; then command him to grasp with both hands between your hands, then go around the place that you have signaled to the whole spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the entire great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk rope firmly, and let them be united by the linen; then work the half of the abscess extended on the linen, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught in the linen, then untie it, and bring the intestine out of the outside of the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it at the incision, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery does you against, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and put the two needles around what you have done in cross that you make to feel; then strain the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will ripen, and let the dead flesh fall by itself; or you cut it when it is thin and ripe, then cure it as it is necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place as it is necessary, and solder the place.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the appearances of ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that ulcers are treated carefully in marshes, and great caution is needed in their treatment, and ancients say that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped away like an ulcer which is in the armpits, and in the groin, and similar places, then one must remove it entirely when it is at its beginning; and when it is large and old, then it is not fitting for you to approach it, because I have never been able to cure any of them; nor has anyone else ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then make the patient's good place for doing the work; then scrape your oncines or ulcer, and shave it from all sides, and remove it entirely without leaving anything; and let the blood flow completely, and firmly press the place with your hand or any thing else, and if the bleeding from the wound goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it as long as the bleeding is extinguished; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have just said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: thus it is stated alone; and one must not touch with iron in these two appearances: that is to say, tympanites and hydrops arch, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this appearance of dropsy which is called "eclights" with medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the sick person is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as thirst and diarrhea and similar things; if you do not touch with iron because there is doubt; and if you see the sick person of strong virtue, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus work: lift the sick person straight up on your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the flank, then take the spine spatula according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be it cut from both parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and still it should not be so inserted that it can come to the intestine when one inserts it, and do not let it bleed; then look if the dropsy is occurring towards the intestines: then it behooves you to make an incision below the third finger bone straight down; and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then have your incision on the left side of the third finger bone; and if it is for the spleen, then on the right, and it should not happen that the patient lies upon the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pull it out, and lift your hand over the whole space between the skin and the syfac as in scouring to the quantity of a fingernail or about; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the eighth place, and this is the place of the water, then draw the fluid out, and insert this instrument from that which this is the form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And is similar to a silver needle, and is of iron or lighter steel, and has in the bottom part I small hole; and where it costs on one side, III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now onto the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than it befits in that hour, by adventure the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls palsied, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then draw the instrument and retain the point, and it is retained now by the heart that stops the hole which is on the syfac, from which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering so, and draw from the point a small quantity; do this no day, and keep yourself from following until there remains not more than a little bit of point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you give him much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and keep him from drinking; and cure him with medicines that dry until he is cured, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At no time are born children who do not have a hole on the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, immediately so that he cannot perceive to all the fine spatulum according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or insert the thin probe of lead, and tie it and hold it thus for III days or IIII and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and by chance, it may not be necessary, because the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, if it is medicated with the cloth of lead as we have said, it will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in its place are bluish, because none are born with the penis at the head of the member, which is why they cannot urinate before lifting their member upward; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, and the head of the member and the scrotum are held as if it were the size of a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should; and keep guard from bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, then the stanchment of those who stanch blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albature comes on the penis, and it is a bad appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant; so it behooves you to prick them with i. one fine needle, and to cut and cleanse all of them, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of putrid color and thereafter, then you must bring it cauterize. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the band is inside the shaft, and has part within the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the band which is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the one outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you cure it together, be sure that the head of the rod is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its rod and where the groin; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then place on top the poultice of honey and flour which is made from the bark of quince trees and of times, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two dispositions together: that is to say, for the removal of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the member is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you put or lead a cane of wood on the member, and piss the patient among; and when the skin is at the head of the member which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you peel it with the instrument sharp, until the ties are untied, and the head of the member is delivered from all sides; and if it is a grievous thing to consider these things, then it is necessary that you peel it with the spatula any point of the head of the member and of the hair; then separate well between the two, and put in the subtle cloth of linen moistened with cold water, that it does not dry up. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of healing; however, when we perform this act willingly, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the easiest to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision of their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the most part of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision with one, two, and three instruments; so they had shears because there are two blades, and by chance if one cuts above, the other remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification that is done with one tool, the point of the member is not always assured; and in the purification of the angle by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born so that they have no need for purification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made with force to the whole length of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so it is equal in I all soul tens; but that the fils be well straight around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the stick so only, and then let him laugh in all the manners that you can; then let him be between your hands straight, and raise the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the stick and blow or heart, and lead it upward until the head of the stick is in; then purify it well of the dirt which is assembled there, then tie the place signed with a double thread, then tie it below I poc to the other lien; and hold it as II does by the second lieeure to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then raise the heart upward gently and lead the head of the stick; then let the blood correct poc and poc, for that is the muedres; and put powder on and on the powder I drapeil glueit d'auef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit with oile roset boin and fres, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it of another cure until it is healthy.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces to the purification is this: the two shoulders should be even and sharp, and the shoulders should also be as large as the palms equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore, it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the place makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they surpass three days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it be left until the abscess softens, and lightly scar it; if you can cut it as gently as possible, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, heal the place with things soft powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if it is cut too much, and it goes up, it will not harm it; therefore, heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Regarding the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of the bladder stone, or frozen blood, or swelling, or flesh mass, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and stretch his belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's groin as much as he can; and therefore it constricts the neck of the bladder to express the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer an extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", because this is its form: and be made of fine silver light cheve, like the feather of a bird; and be the length of a palm and a half, and be fine at the top. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of the urine is that you take the double thread, and tie it to the head the piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the bud; then put the syringe forward up to the bladder, and feel the patient coming to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that by which the lead or where it goes is twisted; then hold the thread to all the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and be aligned the patient. 
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder ailments
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or rot is gathered there, and you see it distilled with sharp waters and medicines, do so to all the instrument which is called 'clepsedre', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the head of the medicine should be such that it stops the rod well without addition, so that if one can drain the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the clyster into the moisture, and draw with the draw that is inside; if you draw the moisture to the clyster, and then reinsert the draw inside; then the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: here it is. 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archut, and the head is higher; and below to the breast where the chies falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in the moisture that you want to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming with a good double thread, and heat the point of the enema on the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the anus, then strain your hand over the bladder at all the moisture coming, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don’t have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put the strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dale, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a knife; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears as if a harenet were there, and it grazes the patient's penis, and it pains them many times, and then it ends; and with many of these leaps the foundations are made; and it is light the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in the old, and it is as the middle for those who are between childhood and old age; and the cure is lighter from those who have a large stone, than from those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, to draw out all the filth which is in the intestines.  
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he often obstructs when seeking out the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and push them out and move them downwards so that the bladder descends to the opening of the urethra and does not rise from its place; then make him sit between your hands equipped, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclining down; then feel and touch inside. If you feel the stone in the space, then haste now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touch of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, apply it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and push it out to where you wish to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where one makes the incision; then put the spatula cutting, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the  hipbones and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right above the stone, and your two should be even or foundation, and let the waist be through the traverse so that it is wide from outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps press the one which is in or foundation, that it leaps out without working; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and margins: if it is cut, it hurts; and if it is soft, like a glant, and round, whose issue is light. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To him therefore where there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you pull upwards with tweezers which are like a file at the head, to force the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath the subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, then enlarge the hole of the opening, and if it does not come out, strain vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut upwards, then the larger one out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be covered, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies or the urine comes back through where the legs cannot hold together; but nonetheless, you force yourself to treat it, or to break it with tongs, until you draw it out in pieces; and when you have finished your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon’s blood, and restrain it, and put above it a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then bind the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, moisten the place well with oil and water, then cure it with diafynicon ointment and basilum ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and by this retention urine is known in such manner that without jumping with the urine: so then you must put in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, so it will corrupt the bladder, and it will rot; then raise the wound of water and of ease and of oil, and help him in all ways that you know, as long as he is healed; and it is necessary that all hours that you care for him, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is or is led by the member, and fixed in it, and the urine cannot pass; so the cure of those that I say thus, that you cut it many times, is excused from cutting through this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus. 
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and have it with three angles fixed into one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the forest in the shaft gently, as far as it reaches the stone; and turn the forest with your hand in the stone up and down, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft.  
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then fractured, and jump out with the urine, and it heals the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod go in place of the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are found in women, and if it happens once, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who unveils the marvels, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deeply hidden than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity appears to this, then it is necessary that you choose a midwife well-knowing, and by pains find one, and if you do not find one, point so much as cast a subtle mire; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her that she make what you command her of the inquiry of the stone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to push her buttocks or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it below her buttocks, and recommend to her that she push her buttocks or with the patient, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is seen appearing and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your hand above the stone or below, and let the tail be first small; then put the tail into the waist, if you feel the stone so acute to the wound as much as the stone can possibly issue, and know that many kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have reins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone hurts you, put crushed vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the stone is extinguished; then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm, and have instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones in men so that you can help you in your work; and if the stone still hurts, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put the powder on the place and bind it with bandages and do not start this again, and leave the stone and don’t touch it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the skin hardens, then return to your work as long as the stone is hard.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramic is nothing else than a gathering of moisture or white syfac, which is below the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and at times is properly in the lining of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have such a pock.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramic is of weakness that comes to the testicles, and is spread that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white such as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.  
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the own cloth, so is the abscess reons with a part of the egg, and for that they think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the genitals and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, it presupposes to the whole intromissoire quarreit, for which its form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then which comes after the introducer, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on something a little high, and puts under him much cloth; then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs next to the heart of the breasts; then take the spatula clean, and cut the skin of the breasts among them down to the long one up to the armpit, and let the incision be all straight when dividing the skin of the breasts until the white silk, and the exfoliate carefully according to your strength; then pierce the soft white full of water with a large opening, and extract all the water, and then put your tweezers, and extend the soft white upwards; and do not touch the heart of the breasts, but only the white one; cut all or in pieces equally the bone next to it subtly, that if you do not cut it well skillfully, it will return the water; and if the work is good on your work, then return it to its place when you have finished the work of the soft white; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the breasts with a suture, then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the skin corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are hanging, suspecting the flow of blood; then cut the onion to all the hanging part, and extract the skin, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound the middle in rose oil; and put outside another wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two sides, and put above doubled cloths, and tie it above all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two straps, and use them of wool padding according to this resemblance and be assembled by stitching in the waist of the breeches, and one of the heads pricks onto the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two chief on the two shoulders, and all assembled the restraint in the loop of the breech; and at times is medicine this branch of cautery in place of a knife of iron, and it is that you prick the cautery scalpel-like, fine, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and be seared as we have said, so that the white juice that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the chop in all the ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more healed; and moves guarding against a decrease of blood, and measures that the works of size; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscesses or discharges of blood or other things, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.  
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to await this work because of its horror, so administer a perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the aquatic root is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with all the spatula wide, and put the perforation long through the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave to run the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you must pour in a pen or the instrument used to drain the water from hydrophics, which form is before mentioned; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or whenever it will, and when it is assembled as before, and so the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the boils
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch, there is fear in many positions, for which it seems to me that one leaves it; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the limbs; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and acute, which is spread as the boils, or percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a grave abscess; and perhaps are some abscesses grievous fearsome and stony, and of flux color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or inflammation of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When this is by our artery, so it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it to your two fingers; and it does not behoove that you touch it.  
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the touch of the two [hands], and one can well make the incision on this semblance, and on the other parts; and that you cut the heart of the coins, then the egg is on top, and the train further down the white syfac, and deliver the suspensor from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already joined with these needle threads, then it is necessary that you draw the egg, and cut it; and if it is in the yolk sac, or those which are inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of that membrane, and cut it roundly.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or its rear, so it is proper that you cut it all and extract the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the boils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a boil wrapped in a wrapping like a barleycorn, with the softening of the boils, and the patient groans loudly when he goes; and the treatment of this disease is as well feared as before, nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the groin down to your two thighs, on all the vessels that are near the penis, and tie them tightly, and stretch them; then cut with a sharp spatula a wide groove through the middle of the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples; then put a needle where the vein has come, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come from, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as with others where one makes a bow, so that no vessels are cut which nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if to all the vessels comes blood, it is necessary to drain the testicles on all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot help itself. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this damage are by the section that comes or sifac, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angres, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the sides; and this rupture is either dou sifac, or of the extension of it, and come these II manners of mouth of causes: or by percussion, or by jump, or by braire, or by lifting of heavy burdens, and by similar things; and the signs when it is the extension dou sifac, is that they have poc and poc, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and are the abscesses equal until towards the parfont, for because the sifac hastens the intestines.  
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the intestines, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears different under the skin near it, because of the issue of the intestine and the body coming out from the opening of the intestine.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are pulled with the abscess, and it is held in, making great pain for the patient, even when it is pressed.
