Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, so one must beware of them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to draw the intestine to his hand inside the wound, if it can enter; then be sewn on his collar between your hands, and lift the hips; then hold the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin long; then put within the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the pus may issue; then scrape the syfac which is under the skin of the groin, until the white syfac hard is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white syfac which is under the skin of the pubic bone, and the second syfac, and depart from what is behind the pubic bone, and between the second syfac; and then move with the right hand inside the heart of the groin, and hold the white syfac on top to your left hand, and lift the pubic bone onto all the syfac towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the pubic bone upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and inquire with your two fingers if there is any intestine enclosed or white syfac hard, and if you find any of these things, put it in the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it into the rear part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as many as there are four; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, about which we have said that it is under the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of two parts; then wrap the hairs of the threads, and tie them together in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter into it, except an abscess may come there; and put straight the thread according to the first long thread of two, and after these two threads leave the syfac which is under the heart of the groin a great one of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the pubic bone carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew and the bone, as we have said before; then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put the thread that we have spoken of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is cauterized the white side which we have said, after the incision, for fear of a decrease of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the thread as long as it hangs by it; and if it delays in falling, then be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this treatise I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the root which is assembled with the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who operate, until the vessels flow; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the bowels as we have said, and it opens them up; and do not allow any of the intestines to go into the anus, and if they do go in, it is little, and repair all hours; and nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, it grows the wound or ulcer, until the intestine goes out; and this happens by the extension of the ulcer that is in the bowels as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen the openings and open; and the cure is by cautery as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies well on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated wide according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the ulcer which is under the skin that goes out, then take the root and put it on the place appearing of the ulcer; and press it at the bottom of the belly, then sew the II appearances of the ulcer above the head of the root, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the root, and do not cut any of the ulcer nor extend the wound or anything else as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines; then cure by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hairs, cleanse it and treat the wound, as long as it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syfac is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in certain men, because the sacks that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; then join the two lips with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin at 3 or 4 stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	of the strapping
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauteries are common in our law, and for this reason I would like to speak little of them in this book; and it is not necessary to learn them except for two ways: one is so that the sick person knows how to respond when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other because we often need cauterization from some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.  
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by traction, we make the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and pliable; then grasp them with your hand until they are set and you feel them no more. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the cauterization of the tail: it is necessary that you grasp the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each side with the knife when you have well scraped them; and leave no point where there is itching or the subtle itching which is on the vessels; and this manner of cauterization is more effective than that done by attraction because in attraction sometimes nothing remains of the testicles, which is why the animal desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men: one if it is that between the two sexes opens as much as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is upon the pointed bone also as a rod and they do (have intercourse). 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of man and woman is that you cauterize all the attached tumors and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of their scrotum, there is no treatment.  
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigine is a carbuncle attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the superfluity of the tetigine in your hand or with tongs, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood flow, then cure it with another cure until it is healed; and to another char that arises at the mouth of the marris, and the limb, and perhaps leap forth, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this they called it anciently "disease of cow".  
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the tendon, and treat it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or by accident by illness that came to it; or it is by a joint char, or by subtle or thick syfac, and it is made in the belly, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and by chance the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the sight of the baile.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppage is near appearing, if you want to it at your two or at the root.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is sick with a subtle fistula, and it is near the two books, then hurry, and do this: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then bring the two books together, as long as the subtle fistula is gone, and cover the place; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the spot, and let the woman lie flat each day, so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the stylus is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with the spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppage is of flesh born, so suspend it to the incison and the cut; and have the medicines blood-thinning, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, along with a good amount of egg; then administer a caine of wide plank, so that the wound may not close; and thus be lengthy, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured by other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the mars comes a new sore, it should be covered according to this manner, if it is not an abscess that has broken open. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is enclosed within the skin, one must not touch with fire.  
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without customary care, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thickened; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are swollen in the anus, and do not appear to smell, except by fire treatment. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then let the uterus be held with forceps, and the womb be cut at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and ginger and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and wax, and make a plaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays there, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply air pumps to the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or elder with old wine, and apply it there.  
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, then care to its place of ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the harsh chief, so it ought to be covered as I have said in the thelul; and then the care until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as ulcers and cancerous abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore it befits me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like abscesses that boil; and if you wish to know the work of iron, then look at whether the abscess is thick at its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not haste thee to pierce, but let him lay still until the pain is calmed; and then make the patient sit upon a seat, and let him have small supports or he may recline, and support his back and join his feet in the direction outside the leg; and let his hips be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them firmly with a good band; then turn the patient toward the right side, and there administer the instrument by which one works the mouth of the throat, so that what comes after will form; and it is necessary when you see administering this instrument, that you put the point first in order to know the depth of the throat, so that he who enters within the instrument does not go more deep than is due, and that it does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the throat with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and let him put the cone of the instrument above, and hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with the hand, then it is necessary to cover it with the chief, with the spatula of lead; and when the pus is emptied, then it is necessary that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green oil; and put the tent from the wound to the edge of the margin, and put outside on the margin and on the knife linen net moistened in water or malves are cooked; then cure after II days of ointment preceding this, until it is healed; and no times raise the margin and the wound by clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristolochia are cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set back in the flesh, then it is necessary that you guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The first thing is for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then she hastens the child to be born; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the head is first, and the second follows; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child comes quickly; because when he descends with his head, then the second follows with him, and the woman is cleansed of her superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes to force the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes upon its belly, or hip, and is converted by chance upon its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the midwife be wise and skillful in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural birth, and the woman is giving birth loudly, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her with oil or fennel that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs a small spatula which has this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine and cut to its nail as long as the moisture which is inside cures; and hold the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with fenugreek mush with sesame oil; then make her swallow and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: so now the child will be born. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are out, then it is necessary that you push them lightly here and there; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up; then tilt the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when tilting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the neck which is before placed, and extract the child, and reset it evenly.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn them back and forth, until they are equal; then grasp the feet and extend them back and forth.  
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	As much as he leaps to his hips, so the command is to take, and do it sneeze from conditions; if he leap further, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take a mixture of althea and sesame oil and melted gum, and grind everything together in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until under the ribs; and when she is softened underneath, then make a collar of myrrh and put it underneath, and let her stay for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently take her belly, because now the child leaps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts the midwife her hands here and there; then she lies on his neck, and the feet hang down, and lie supine on the bed; and he bends his hands here and there, and then takes the hands above the belly, and removes the cushions below, until it is prepared downward; and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them gently, then moves the belly upward, then puts his hands; and thus the child here and there; and commands the woman to hold on until the child emerges.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child who comes out with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman lie down and go; if she cannot go, then have her lie on the bed and spread her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on the seat, then try to bring back the hand; and hold the child according to the natural form, and have her sneeze, and command her to suckle as long as the babe will. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on his neck, and having spread out his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient holds his hand, then turns it back and forth, and lightly; and when it is even, he puts on the musculature layer of elevation and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to move it back and forth; and when you have done this, place her on the seat, and command her to stand up; and she will sneeze.  
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner to the whole secondine, so cut the secondine to your finger, as long as the moisture is emptied; and if the child may put up on its face and on its neck, so cut from the bud, that it be not retained, and die the child; then put the child inside, as long as you have put it as it should be, and command to the woman that she does not strain herself at all times: therefore it will go lightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and they do not live, if one can name them; I know these, that they be multiplied, and they are divided by the syfac who devises them, which is joined to the bud; and sometimes they come forth as naturally as all under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out violently, do the cure as we have said, and let the surgeon be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do thus as he wants to live. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marsh I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its sage glorious, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this because by chance similar things happen; so do what is appropriate.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and be her shoulders inclined down, and her legs raised; and the minister take hold of her from two parts, or she be tied to the bed so that she not be moved by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then oil her hands with these oils and these mixtures; then put them into the womb gently, then put where she puts the pins that are suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appeared that it descends on its head; then put the pins in its eyes or in its neck or in its mouth or in its palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, then put it or prick it and at the side ribs; and it is necessary that he hold the pin with his right hand, and put the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and put it to all his hand gently, and put the pin in any one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place against the other bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them equal in moving from one side to the other, so they may move smoothly, and let the bones be toothed so they hold together, as is shown here: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains a part, so he anoints the bail some of his oil, and puts them in that part, and pulls the other part; and if there remains none, he puts this one or higher place, and does this as long as it escapes all outwards. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward of the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you must wrap it on the drapery, until it is all healed; then cut at the joint of the foot or at the ankle, and thus you should do with the other hand, and with the two feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is strained in its exit, or it has a sharp head assembled, then you should put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the sharpness; or you will round it with the instrument that is called "almidach," so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the child has a large head naturally; and then draw out the bones with pliers, and if the head leaps out and it is strained to the forceps, then be split, as long as the moisture that is where it came out earlier; and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture comes out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the marrow is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, then it behoves you to draw it out with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and make the belly or the breast, as long as the moisture that is there corrects; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put the bail of your hand into the cavity, and lead it up to the mouth of the cavity; then put the hook in or out, and lead it further; and if the mouth of the cavity is narrowed because of an abscess that has come, then it does not behoove to work on it, but it behoves to administer moist and fatty things; and administer plasters, and sicca in soft and moist water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, follow what we have said in a living child; and if you cannot do this, then treat it by pieces, and leave nothing of the secondine.  
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if they administer to him what we have said about abscesses, those that come in the marshes; and if bleeding comes, it should be put into sharp restraint, and administered other cures.  
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one fetus had been killed, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the belly, and it inflamed so that it opened, and began with great pus discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I pondered long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much astonished, because this one whose belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cauterized the wound, and in tracing my hand over the bones, as long as the woman was in better condition; and she lived long afterward, and it seemed to me a little bow at that place; and I do not remember this chapter otherwise than because when the master finds a strange thing, he should know how to put help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the pressor, which we have in the books; and to 2 turns of 2 bones of the 2 limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle in restriction, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be of large size, and the edges of the trees it must be, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the mortise to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, in its semblance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood shaft, according to the appearance of pliers; and it has two jaws two adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and two arms wide; and when you see open the vagina with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and legs open, then put the two jaws together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done to pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the girl does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the mirrors have shown them, so much more hasty is the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you do not have it displayed, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she leaps through this, well. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not so, then take a pot, and make I pierced or covered, and I put herbs that may open the mouth of the marsh, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put a chain or pierced pot, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and the reign until the vapors come within the marsh; then I make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more strength, command the midwife that she moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in liniment of altea, and then put it into the nature, and seeks the secondine; and when she will have found it, she grasps it and extends it little by little straightly, so that the marrow does not fall at the extraction; but it must be moved lightly to right and left, and then pulls; if it comes and loosens itself. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare is tight shut, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not use the milking; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then clisterize it with ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it will pass and put it back, and will come forth; but nonetheless, when she gives birth, if it comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleaches the sick person. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary fumigations suitable to those things: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the flowers and the second is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the chief subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide on the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and the tinder as long as it is wasted, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped up with a subtle syfac: so it befits the midwife that she pierce that syfac at its due, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the lacement so that it does not touch; then puts on soft linen in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not close up, then put upon the opening a piece of plantain, and leave it for several days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stupefaction comes from the tightening of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that tightening; if it is cured, as we have said about the cauterization of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that come from below the foundation are knotted, and larger than those that come from the side of the foundation or in the space between the two parts, whether it is one fistula or more; and when that knotting is old, it works, and still moisture arises white or subtle bowel, and sometimes these fistulas pass through; and they are known by those who have them or by discharge or windiness when the patient defecates, and perhaps in some cases they jump out. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and reach up to the junction of the hip, and up to the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula going through to the base, and not going through: and it is that you put your middle finger or base, and put a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, put in a tent of fine lead, or horse hair, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your touch; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from a purulent discharge or flatulence or worm, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it spurts urine and cannot be closed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes up to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain in the surrounding area, then it is that there is a bow there, and there is no use of medicine or treatment by ointment; and in these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish wonders who intervene in them. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither young nor old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and raise his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined to his belly; then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is twisting, as long as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, then you should put your index finger there, and feel when it presses against it; and be discovered or you feel between your finger the tendon or the flesh, then you know that it is pierced; if you don't work on it at all one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can therefore say that one cannot heal some well, but this happens rarely; and the help one makes, if one carefully heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and puts all hot in the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred hairs are burned, which are similar to an eye feather; and then cure with damp bandages in butter, as long as those hairs are gone out, then cure with healing ointment char and binding. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, that is good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	Se this, otherwise cannot be healed; and if it is caught between, and does not pierce to the root which is at the base, and between your two do and the tent a thick covering of flesh or syfac, and you see the fistula as follows the covering out of the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward ahead of the tent, and then the cautery afterwards, until it comes to the head of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and fall; then pull those hairs that seem like a feather of an owl, and remain nothing. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sore goes forth, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because the fire cautery brings together II good things: that is to say, the burning of these attached parts, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of tender wounds in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound bleeds, and if it is a char burned in the hollow; then the cure of wounds from blows by applying hard charcoal, and they are the dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes as far as to the bottom of the foundation, and is moved away from the body, then you put your finger or foundation in it and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or the syfac or chars, where it is close to piercing, if there is no other way except by faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III manners: whether you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as before; and do not go too deep in that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and comes the egestions by the way willing; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the world since it is cut from its foundation, or by tent or by another appointed instrument; then mundify the char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or costs on the foundation near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one twisted thread into two, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you push your finger or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two ends together, and hold them to each other, and leave it for a day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads close these scars that are between two, and heal. Then treat the wound until it is sutured and healed.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make a cut covering it if it is too deeply embedded, and then cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spathe-shaped spine from which one makes a fistula is very difficult on one side and trenches; and on the other side, no, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are inside the foundation, as a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, they contain blood, and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and also contain or a little bit of clear water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of these who have them inside the foundation is that you command the patient to lie down in chambers so that the foundations are felt, and the threads appear; then hasten, and you can take them with tweezers, or you hold them with your finger, then cut them at their roots; and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, you take them with a drape, or with cotton, or with a piece of chamois; and you extract them to your two fingers, then cut them, and powder above some hot powders that are in their place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, you enema the patient with a biting and harsh enema to wash what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient sits up, and if the threads are out of the foundation, the cure is light; and it is that you take them with your finger or with tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and he fears incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take a thread twisted and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest; and then leave him until they are dry, and when they will be dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until he is cured.  
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of veins in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you remove to the point of a spatula or your fingernail the bark from above, which does not leave it moist; then treat it as long as it heals as it is fitting; and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and be scraped; then treat it as long as it is healed. 
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small appearance faulty before the body, and goes much into them; and sometimes it finds it cold, and feels it as if dead of fright, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than another part. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane of an ostrich feather, or a vulture feather very strong, and put that cane upon the  bone, as long as the purple circles stain the bone all around; then turn your hand to the whole cane until you cover the whole bone, and put it in its entirety, and root out the bone from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a canine of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it too deeply, for to keep hold of the two, and move pressing. And if you see, so cauterize the furrow, as it is in front or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At no time is a clister made of silver or lead, or iron melted or woven; and at no time are these instruments made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore whom one administers in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large as it is above wide, where the belly is tied according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a severance where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and on one side II pierced, and on the other I; and the belly where one puts medicines of a bladder of animal or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole I must of space, then put in these holes I thread strong of twisted thread X or whichever around, and assemble the belly as it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the lie has the instrument before a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with clyster of oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently; then squeeze the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all visible, then extract the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to go out, let it go as much as it can; and if he sleeps all night straight through, then it is more help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema it in illness of a falling belly, and the medicine hastens to work, then restart it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or abscess, then let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster by which the skin is restrained. 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the thrust of a stone, and the cut of a sword and knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; which are done according to their places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I shall begin with wounds of the head simple, because remembrance comes in its chapter.
