Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, so take care if it is of a stone cutting or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is great, and you doubt strongly of an abscess hot: so make him bleed from the cephalic immediately even if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the part numb; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and fatty meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to bleed, let his meat be lessened, and drink no wine, nor eat any flesh; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in vin stipite; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, that I shall say a little later; and if it has been moved by heat, put on some ointment, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with tents, then bring them together by sewing, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered of bone, and it hangs, and holds only by a bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and wheat cooked, also as poultices, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut away all the rot, and throw it out, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without doubt, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.  
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put into this powder which unites as if the fire had moved them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins to all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime, when one lacks incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has not cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has cauterized the wound, even in being there, do not put on this powder; but put on some ointment digesteds, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it swells up; then cure with other cures until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you here later about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of these is with the brain, which is the most high member; but let the medicine be warm, such as chalz washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucie washed also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so sew it and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of bowel, then pierce or lower them; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize as necessary is; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the vein, and the conductor is kept, by which the flesh goes, then sew the heart on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then restrain it carefully, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then stitch it; and if there are pieces of bone, if you can remove all of them, but those that you cannot have, then leave them as long as the wound rots, and be free and align the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then put powder on top of the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a sword or spear wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, see if from the wound airiness comes as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, do not put any powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not remain open, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it two times a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there comes not spasm, nor bad tremor of heart, nor straining of breath; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat then with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; treat the wound as one must. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, then the cure of that which is in front; if it is large, sutured; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deep into the bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and pull out the splinters if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, so that it will help to remove them; and for other wounds in the other limbs, judgment as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the belly's derangement
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	A rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerve of the intestines comes out because of insertion; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound because of this one puts back the intestines with care if not they are put in hot to cold; because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, they go in less easily, and for that reason a medium wound is worth more because of this one returns the intestine to its place that other II And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IV ways: the II sutures common happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the body and II other sutures proper are common to the other wounds; and nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines has come out, and it is dangerous to put things back, then it is by one of the two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water only, or you cook in boiling water squinant and cypress and spike, and arouse the intestine until the swelling is removed; and at no time do this restraining, and are muedre that awe alone for deflating.  
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and well-cooked herbs, for by this is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument that one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to heal the wound, that no one should cut it without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting it;  so cut inside into the curve and outside not, and see here the shape. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have protruded, put it back in place according to its natural form, if you are able, because it is of great importance.  
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, it behooves you to make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and pelvis higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention on that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus it behoves to administer what I say in large and medium wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put those that are visible to you, then take in your hands the minister pitiful who holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of suturing, and it is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the top of the wound I space, and there put a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the II heads of the siphac the IV together; then strain a double thread around the needle of the two parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound again, and then leave I space, and there put another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason it is necessary that they be moderate; and it does not suit to put the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not prick the patient when sleeping, and put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles for the muscles to hold, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there suffices one needle or II.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound healed up to 15 days, and I treated it, and he was well.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in that place where one found none, nor any medicines; and I put sens more on the wound cotton old twice a day, and I washed it with water of honey until it was healed.  
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and put it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the core straight through, leave the tip of the shaft where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside out; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furriers do with pelts, and that you leave one end of the shaft on one side, and take it back on the other, until the stitching is complete.  
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suture, which Galens says properly, is like any wound, which brings the two parts together naturally, and apply one chief of the syfac to the other chief, in this manner: stick a needle or chief of mirach prochiene, and make it pierce that place alone, and leave the two chiés dou syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner one, at the two chiés dou syfac; then make it pierce both from the outer part to the inner one, at two other chiés dou mirach that are on the other side; and this is the middle manner of suture and the most common.  
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this word, and no one witnesses it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corroi; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the others of the belly.  
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even as the arrow has moved it, so put back the intestine, and the gut; then put on powder enjanrant char, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and stitch the thread, and be soldered the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, so put on, as soon as it begins to giter bowe, old cotton, and move it II times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make commonality with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten linen lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the wounds, and under the buttocks; and if they feel pain or rot in the belly, and many times happen, then give clisterizes of black wine, and even if the rot comes to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when this is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is damaged, and that is because of the planting of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.  
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon jumps from the wound, put it back as far as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or brown, then you should tie the black part so that bleeding does not come from it, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and place the two ends hanging from below the wound until outside to align the extraction when the tendon falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, for I saw a man wounded in his belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it festered and became a fistula, and through this were passing excrement and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until he was healed, and the edges joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sew, I doubted that the patient would have poorly in his belly; and there was no evil, but stayed in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and they said any experimentors that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take fremis to big heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the fremis has covered the mouth, so put it on the II lips, so that it strains its mouth upwards; and then cut the head, and it stays so that it cannot undo, then put I other fremit after in the same manner as before, until the wound is all taken care of; and sew the wound.  
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief if it inflames in the intestine, and no nuisance comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine of a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is very thin, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of linen subtle twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it at the rupture; and this way of sewing of threads there is nothing but according to the way of hope and promise; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no other thing nor health, except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and even when it is closed and healed. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knotted false boil and white, in which one feels no pain, and is also shaped like the quill of an eye; and sometimes it is clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the IX causes: that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to be born; or there is too much bowe; or the wound is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	So it is necessary that I teach you the cure of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sciatic nerve, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the sides, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, so take a tent of iron or iron, if the fistula is straight, so the one; and if the fistula is crooked, so the circle with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends follows the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well search it with tents, so clistize it by one of the holes, because the moisture passes from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then the one searches wisely to your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is covered in depth, and ask well the patient of the pain that he feels at pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have said to you, so operate according to what I have said to you, and remove the festering and the rotten things that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep of right place, it is necessary that you operate in depth, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in medicine sharp, and they put them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is remained at the bottom; and then put ointment invigorating healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so operate on it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves do not affect the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the king as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure with things of flesh until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns in the way before, know that you are not well gone to the end: uncover and seek as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, it is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that is not so, know that the corruption is too far advanced, that you cannot fix it; if there is nothing else to leave to nature; and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, do not leave any one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut both the moisture and flesh, and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound a thing hindering rot, and let it remain until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a great bone, like a leg or thigh, wait only for the corruption to be entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corruption, and comes up to the marrow of the bone; it must be soired and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is solid; and I will tell you about an abscess that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about XXX years, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the substances came to the leg, and became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open it; but the physicians by their folly operated so much that the abscess opened, and they corroded much of the matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many holes that all flowed pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated him for about II years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what flowed through the holes a great deal of flesh; and the skin of the young man became red, and had a citrine color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these perforations, and then I searched all the perforations, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore proceeded, and bored into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came to the inside bone; I was amazed by what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had removed; and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but could not close it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to close the place; but I could not more than I bored into one palm's breadth of the bone, and the tract was throughout its whole length, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and healed quickly, and it did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him.  
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often took place, but he was healed entirely, and in the place of the bone there grew a hard cartilage, and he was of good disposition and had no discomfort or contrary thing at all, neither in going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it is fitting to be treated in this manner: take linen and strain it at the head of the bone that gapes, and command someone that he extend it upward; and put another band of thicker linen above the first linen, and tie it over the flesh which is below the bone, and extend the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to be, that the bone does not pierce the flesh; and put a splint or a plank under the bone for to cover the corrupted flesh; and it is fitting to be as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is rotten and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh completely; then put a piece of charcoal underneath, and then with a thread from one side to the other place the corruption, and let the thread be long enough for the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and suture the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to do but to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or in the finger of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corruption, how it opens for you; and clean it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve does not oppose you; and know that there are many instruments to cut these bones, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their thinness, and their largeness and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip oneself with each kind of work its instrument; and know that practice will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so plan the instrument that you need according to what it requires.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be affected from inside or outside; and when you have medicine those corrosions by the treatment of medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the evil, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems that it is burned by fire, and after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb, and takes throughout the body; if you hurry to cover, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no other remedy than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut all the foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or treating the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister from the lower ligament, and another minister the upper ligament, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ligaments a spatula wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then cut or treat, and put on each side I bandage of linen, so that the treatment does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the bleeding occurs when you operate, then cauterize the place well, or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the limb injured with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackening that seemed burnt by fire, and that corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned in his hand's heel, and he came to me, and I put on things refractive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he urged that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of recovering the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the virtue of man was weak; and he despaired of everything, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have this story told only for the sake of what is done otherwise, if it is necessary.  
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and leaks, and the pus spills out, like vessels; and the skin which is above is as thin as silk handkerchiefs, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "boil", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone or marrow, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin so is that you cut all around the skin, even when it is as thin as silk handkerchiefs; and does not hurt for its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not in perfection, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clyster thus: see if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, therefore clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is thus made: take asafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and put the cure into a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some of this according to your necessity, and make it in water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and hold the anus closed; and leave the medicine inside for II hours, then extract it by straining; do this many times until the breast is softened, and the stench is removed; and at one time, clysterize with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from the vine wood, and pour water over them, then filter it, and clysterize with it, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey or in which there is a bit of powdered litharge; or you clysterize with honey and sweet wine, because honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine makes it open; and when you have done this, and you are convinced that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with what makes flesh grow in it, and which is made with diaphana plaster, and mixed with rose oil and wine; or you clysterize with some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have spoken or treated in the ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the clyster can not enter, then enlarge it with iron a bit, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then cut it and leave only that place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening which emits stench is above, then cut lower than where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, do not let any meat be inserted; and if you cannot cover the breast as you wish, then arrange it so that the bow runs to the lowest point that it is at, for when the bow is in place, do not let any meat be inserted and if you cannot cover the breast as you wish, arrange it so that the bow runs gently downwards, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take solidifying medicines to put on the wound, and stay under the linen sheet that covers the entire wound; then cut as forcefully at the edge of the breast as possible, a little wider than the first time; then apply ointment above the other sheet according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound so as to align the bow, and do not remove the larger sheet outside for many days once; and the one that is on the edge of the breast, often removed in order to take out the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it be venom or a little or enough, digested or indigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when the medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that rises on the wound, then know that the breasts will be healed soon, and approach health; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other sheet, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bent badly after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venoms come after a long time, if it does not trouble you of the health, because the health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite; and if a breast boils after many days, know that the breasts do not close well; and if the breasts are slow to close, and they are far apart, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, because there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same is made with honey cooked when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue the cloth, and lay it on the breast, and at times administer a long scalpel, and roots of lilies of heaven, which are also like flour from vetiver and centaury; and use either simple or composed: grind them, and make powder of them, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the wound is prolonged, and is not healed by this cure, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in limbs; so the cure of fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or the foot, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then it comes the abscess boils, and runs and eats flesh until it eats to the root of the nail, and by chance it eats it all; and come the sores until the bone, so much that there comes pain pungent, and is the limb of the two wide, and is the color flushed. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut to it.  Cut all the superfluity which is remaining from the angle, then cauterize the wound after. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and it begins to prick, and the blemish, then you should put the head under the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and put it upwards, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put above the remaining flesh medicines ardent and corrosive to remove all; then cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and heal because as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see the two to be corrupted, then cut it in one of the ways as has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and pushed, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first; then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and guard so that the cutting does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on top which soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand's source
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is one where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us different. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any nut of the two does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is so light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so hold him to be cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be at the last our, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, then cure it until it is sound.  
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sutures that come to the two together come by birth, or by joining of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the solder so that the parts return according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not rejoin; or you put between two pieces of subtle wood, until the bones are joined, as is fitting. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When joining comes to none of its two with the palm, so join that joint as it is fitting.
des vils	of the villages 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities, that come in many members of the body; and more happen in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than to others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging with coles, and then the salve of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two manners: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it completely.  
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is done in this manner: first rise the leg with hot water very strong, until the large vein be softened, then restrain the leg of the sick person from above the hip down to below the knee; then cut the vein in I place, or in II or in III, with a wide incision, then cleanse and pull out black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtues of the sick person can bear; and then tie it up, and command him to be covered with meat stewing black jelly; and recommence the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and hurt the sick person. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the leg is done in this manner: place the patient's leg on a table if there is much hair, then put it in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut above the vein from the top of the knee to the heel, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a scalpel and scrape the vein on each side until it appears when one feels it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then push the point beneath until it is raised from the skin, and then place it lightly on the knife, and then cut again in another place upwards of three finger widths; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then raise it to the point as you did before, and place it on another knife as you did at first; then make another cut, or more if needed, then raise it and cut at the top of the foot, then pull and raise it up to the second cut; then extract from cut to cut until it is all out, then cut; and if you cannot pull and raise it, put a strong double thread needle through it all and tie and pull it, and push it under the point, and turn your hand on both sides until it comes out; and guard that it does not break, for if it breaks, one cannot pull or raise it, and it brings great annoyance to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it in a twist, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cauterizes the vein is curved and does not cut, so that it only cauterizes the vein; and it is of a thick curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be as thick as we have said, and here is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land; and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of rot that comes from under the skin, like it comes from inside the body serpents and worms, nestled between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its color, and begins the vein to flow out, like the root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
