When the bone breaks open, it is necessary that you envelop it around a piece of wood from one and a half to two inches, and tie it, and leave the wood on the leg, and all times when it is pointed to the outside, you envelop it around the wood, and tie it; and if it is too long, you cut a part of it, and envelop the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it enters back into the flesh, and brings forth an abscess and rotting where it is, and a bad illness; therefore, for this reason, it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remain on the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of five palms long, or of ten, and one man came to me once, whose it was ten palms long, and when you cut it, he brings out the root of the tendon, and pierces it all the way down, so that everything comes out; and be emptied the matter which is inside, and administer at the place medicines preventing rotting any day, then cure it like abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at times this vein appears again, and even when it opens in the foot's joint or foot, and there comes much pus, and from which it flows blood; treat it as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the end of limb to limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and jumps further; and it is generated by decay of some humors, like come worms and snakes and debris and roundworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, one can only do so when he goes: therefore, it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong linen band tightly, then cut on top and treat the wound, and if the worm is driven into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, restrain the eyebrow below it, then cut on top, and treat the wound; and it is necessary to use the patient of cleansing of the body with medicines solutives for the humors that are carried, and avoid eating meats that cause putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen those whom I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she discovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I saw after a while it rise as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, like living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and moved to the shoulder, and then a little after it corrupted throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning around her body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I wished many who well have wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and veins discovered, and for this reason appeared that constricted windiness; and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it above and below firmly, and then cut upwards as much as the constriction of wind caused it to be; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with those who expel winds, such as fetid pills, and serapine pills, and similar ones. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some that have large points, and small, and hair, and joined; and those that have II angles, and those that have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one that falls in any limb falls according to II manners: or in principal member falls, such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestine, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls then in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appear to you: then it is necessary that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deep, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and leaps the syfac which is on the brain, is when there is scotomy and suddenness and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perchance blood from the nostrils, or the ears; and perchance it loses the speech and the voice; and leaps from the wound a moist white seeming to wool, and leaps also as burnt flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty; and perchance the seventh moves also like the pulse, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know therefore without doubt that death approaches.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move its body is that without pains of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns color, and gasps loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls in the covering of the breast, it is near the ribs; and he feels great pain and great sorrow and sighs; and he moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls in the stomach, by chance it throws out of the wound some thing of undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls in the belly, and through the intestinal rout it throws out a piece of fiber, there is no hope for cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and the urine comes out mixed with it, and the patient feels great pain; know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, as the arm and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the auxiliary and the spine of the back and the thigh and the hip and the legs, and the seeming members, are safe according to more dispostitions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason that you do it otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man with an arrow that shot or pierced in the root of his nose: I took it out, and pulled it from the other side below the ear fat, and he was cured without feeling at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And treat with one game an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye below the paper below, and the arrow was put back, and I could not touch it except the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, at all light iron without ears; the game was safe, and he did not have any bad accidents. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treat an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully as much as I drew it out, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow in a man, that was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then when he had passed thirty days, it did not change its position; I cut on the arrow, and burned it, and treated the wound, and there was no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to the man who has an arrow shot or behind, and the wound is sewn up; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural disposition, nor finds annoyance in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And there is another man, whose arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sutured; and remained so suffering great pain; and many other similar things.  
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow to the man of princes the king, who it was lodged in the middle of his thigh, and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called for treatment after three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it to be a very fine tent, and I did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the emplasters on my hands for several days, and sutured the wound straight, and kept the patient there a long time until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his flesh; and he told me. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive and sharp for many days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow hardening in place; then I placed it in the opening of the wound with that medicine sharp, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it pierced well the extremities for four months, and then widened so much the wound that I put pliers into it, and held it from one side and the other, and it could not come out; therefore I did not cease to tinker and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day the pliers well made, according to what its form will appear at the end of this chapter, until I treated it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it therefore, and it was sutured the wound, and it was healed the patient entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take everything; but the wise masters compare with very little thing, and with what is present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to the descent of strange things which happen in this art.  
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not from the members where they are fixed further than according to II manners: or by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that is farther by where it enters, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and it is never any time now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it as long as the bone is carried around, and soothe the exit; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it like that for some days, and move it every day; and when it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around it with a fine needle, until the skin around it is opened, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and it goes until one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it until it is even after some days, because if the arrow comes until the syfac, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone, and does not come to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then the engine of milk. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be removed further, then administer  a poultice around it, as I have told you; then care for the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body so that one cannot see it, then search for it all over; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then cut as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at what it holds, then remove the flesh which is stuck between its two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can draw it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, so that you will draw it out more painfully. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then place it until its end is softened, then treat it, for the extraction hurts less.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes you act contrary, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put every means by which you can draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one does not see anything of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it apparently: cut therefore upwards, as long as the pliers can take it, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.  
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, so that it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it is drawn out; and if there is an arrow shaft in it, thrust it completely into the shaft; and if the shaft is broken, and you see to administer a thrust, administer the instrument head first, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then thrust it, and if the arrow shaft is stuck, thrust the instrument head first again, in order to facilitate the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it is required. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs and it is near, and you can cover above, se it cover; and keep from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if need is; and cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to an eye's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the head of the arrow is like that of the feather of a bird, to put it at the point of the shaft, just as this one is in shape. 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers for cutting and holding is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI in the head, that is to say: II veins which are after the ears, which are called the "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in II temples appearing; and II veins which are in II tear ducts of II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the head of the two; and the II jugulars which are on the neck; and the II veins which are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins which are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that one commonly heals are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the ribcage, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast," and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side of the ribcage, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the bone, and it is the one that one heals, which opens clearly on the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two veins in the arm; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the curve of the pocket on the left side; and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "the great", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins under those.  
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs, and migraines; and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependence upon the head: then find where on your back, and where you feel the pulse under your back, then seize it; then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein above, and cut both the skin and the vein well two fingers of the traversing, and make blood issue as much as you see; then strain and tie, until it is cleansed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the II arteries that are in II temples, it is good for old migraine, and acute, and accustomed ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp as the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as I say: and it is that the patient constricts his neck, until the II veins appear clearly; and feels the two pulses below his chin, and then reigns in them; then raises the heart above the vein on his right index, and puts the lancet below, and raises the vein up, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and makes a cure of blood according to your need; then unties the patient, and puts his right hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton; and then the scab forms, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cutting and their extraction, as the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the vein of the cephalic for ailments of old face, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fossor," whose form is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and steady with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never work it with a broad flame.  
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right that the flames be too large; and  the vein should not be treated crookedly, because the bone is near, and by chance the flames will break the vein when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in two tears helps the eyes, and to the forehead, and to the cheek, and to the corner of the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then he bleeds, and whether the bleeding is from a travers, a little short of the flame, or a little long, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then do a correction of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for fever and headaches, and ailments of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his collar, then strains his nose with his left hand, and takes a fine long thread, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not let it flow too far, and make blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the thread: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II veins helps in the treatment of the arm, and at the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and scurvy, and erosion, and herpes, and scabies; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient restricts his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on top of the head of the sick person, and the sick person sitting on a bench, then open the vein of the length a little widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary; then do another part in the other vein, then untie the linen, and restrain the two veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and let it remain until morning, that the wound may be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the veins of the limbs 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins of the lips above helps in ulcers in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and for toothaches and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right side and the other on the left, and know them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: cut therefore both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each part, and also of the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bloodletting of the cephalic vein, and it is to the loosening of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeding are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side one black vein: bleed therefore one and the other, and do not go too deep in them, because below are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut by which commonly one is bled are opened in two ways: either they prick at all the flame well wide or with a subtle knife like sharp cutters, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is need to open the veins that are healthy and flat of large visible blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of olive flame.  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to cut wisely, and that he avoid the artery which is under.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he strikes the ground, and a run of blood comes, then it is necessary to cauterize it as I have said; and it must not be pricking the flame, but cutting like an awl. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basil does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another one; or you wish none of its vein, or you heal in its place the vein removed from the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cup to the flame anointed, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the place of the vein, then so it is necessary that you draw out the arm, that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse; then mark the place with an incision, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame in your left hand; and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: escape therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulge upwards like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your hand on top lengthwise, then remove your hand if the skin is stretched, which often happens; bind his arm, and leave him so, and do not move him. And be fearful, and do not move him until he is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the loin is not stained and it pains you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the vein; and stain the loin.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of fig, and make it thin, and take one half and tie it well up to the other day; if it stays unmoved, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the stanching is not grievous in more positions for the small place of the wound, and the power of the binding of the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below, for that it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the healthy one that he make himself warse for the nerve that is below, and if it point too much em parfont, and it trueve the nerve, and it inflates and the saints be greased, and by adventure it cannot heal; and this nerve opens mult of times, and if it does not open in any man for its subtility, then it behoves that you the vein of the instrument anesil; and eschui the nerve to your pooir. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head helps so much that it draws blood from the head, and it helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in pricking at the olive branch or the myrtle branch, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has no nerves nor arteries. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and it does not matter if one fails the first time, and one begins again; and by chance it swells the limbs in some men, as long as one fails the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, is that bloodletting is administered only to keep health and to avoid future diseases; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins which are or: that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and it must be bled at the beginning of Lent on foot, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be bled on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered to the sick has no determined time, but when it is needed day or night, at all hours and at all times; and it does not befit to bleed children up to XIV years, nor a woman carrying until the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some one wants to bleed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that they evacuate the intestines with a light enema, if they have much mucus retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous impurities harmful to the principal members; nor let him who is too full of meats or drunk, as long as he is, nor those who are dropsy; and if worse one bleeds after colic passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and multiplication of labor in a woman, and childbirth, and watchfulness, and fasting, and that which all virtue, or by thing of arms or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if he is full, through meats and drinks and medicines, if you have his power; then enter into a bath, if anything does not prevent it, in order to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist on the third part, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be lazy and joyful, and let the bleeding one be higher than him who bleeds, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the linen above halfway, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell up and you feel them; then moisten the bleeding one's flesh with a little bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein below the point where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not escape and fail at the time of pricking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are as thick as cords in the groin, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts the flame on them, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if it opens the vein, it is the wound too narrow, because of which it behoves the surgeons to be aware of these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, it begins again a little below where it was or above the swelling, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let him rest one or two days, and not tie up his arm: for by chance pus may come; and do not enter the bath, then begin the bloodletting if he wishes it; and if the wound is small, or the vein thin and subtly, and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, so pierce the same wound directly to the whole stream; and make a little stitch, as long as the limb is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin again with bloodletting, and put above a bit of oil, because it closes the body of blood, and is mixed in this place the oil that the flesh; and thus administer the oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, for to stop the course of blood; and the same thing triacle and bowe of them, when one puts it on the place; so subtle the wound and parts when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there come an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is only drained at the time that the opening of the vein is small, so hasten, and put on top sponge moistened in water and a little hot, and restrain one hour; and you must do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days no blackness or greenishness, it will not harm him; and if you see, put upon anything of aloes or myrrh applied in juice of calamine, monstastre, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance at the wound of the basilica: put therefore your hand on it, and if you find its place soft to the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid that you put on it anything of those we have said, because by chance it lacks the artery; but let it have .i. dry plaster to harden the place, then the cure of another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, let it shrink until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is plump and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little by little and often, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this way of bleeding is safe from hemorrhage and nerve damage, and is better than bloodletting done with a long or wide [instrument]. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body is ill with the bloodletting, it is necessary to give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if it is feverish, treat it with the blood III times or IV And if it is of cold complexion, warm before the bloodletting moist bread in muced syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pains at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moistens broth of meat, and fragrant syrup subtly, and uses the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm, and another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he should bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be bled from another place, then he must be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already exhausted, and it brings fever; so it befits to draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it flows in pameson; then when you reward all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon his pulse when he is healthy, that death may not come into the place of pameson, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it befits not when you see to untie the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the vein is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is curved, that he extend the arm all the way, for this would be bad; but leave it as long as it heals a second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out, and place upon the little bit of flesh returned to sharpness, and press gently.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and don't constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it heal in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein taken from the arm is bled at the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the bone is red; then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then it is bled through, neither broad nor long; and let the opening be wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if one cannot draw it out, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood to run in the water, until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is put there more in winter than in summer; and the bleeding of this vein is safer from all other veins, as there is no artery or nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is inflated, if one sees it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it through entirely, it does not harm anything; and do not go too deeply, because the nerves are under all skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot exit. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as is necessary, then put oil and a cloth on top of the vein to soothe it well, and so do for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of them in the left hand is as good for the disease of the mouse, and do all just as I have told you towards right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the saffron is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the knees, and retention of flowers, and disease of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his ointment are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it throbs, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; so treat where more prominent vein, or at the ankle, which one deems best. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you seize it on the foot, guard the nerves that are below, and seize it by traversing it as in cutting; and let the flames be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot pull out with the seizing, put the foot in the water and let the vein be well drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision is necessary for the first time, it should be recommenced a second time above a point, because the wound is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same with the opposite foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the ankle's lower part, and its incision benefits the pain in the hip when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein are such that the patient enters the bath and is strained above the ankle IV fingers by twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then you heal it in all ways that you can, and across; and it is better that you heal it than that you cut it, because the veins are dry, and they are very well healed to human hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy any vein of him who opens or back of the foot, and towards the small hip, and guard the nerves; and make so much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the bond, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now cured.  
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches cups are made of horn, or resin, or glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is meant to heal is in two ways: either it is with fire or without fire; and cupping which is done by cutting and the extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, so one is entirely on the top of the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in the two ribs of the neck; and the cup below the chin; and the cup on the two shoulders; and the cup above the hips; and the cups between the two arms; and the cups on the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not deal with blood, except for small veins which are spread in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as much as one does from bloodletting of a vein; and it should not be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to bleed, or for customs, we shall bring them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are such who when they have need to bleed, they have a heavy head; and so there are some who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and they swell their tongue, and rach blood; and so there are some who dream, and see through the blood, and corpses and deaths and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed from the month, we command them to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the vein helps with the pain in the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this phlebotomy is in place of the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have catarrh, because this does much harm to them; and for this reason it is not necessary that old people use it, nor those who have or cold head diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who heals from it often becomes oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for that reason it is good for the treatment of the hip, and for opening the channel of the armpit, and for all things, and for repletion; and one should not block it too much, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause blockage in the stomach or heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The belches as II ribs of the neck are worth to pains of the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and to the strangulation, and to the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the vein of the basilica; and you must command to the patient that he expresses his hand when putting, that he does not cut the artery, and does not come a flow of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations below the chin are good for mouth ailments, and gum disease, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for the illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations of the veins are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient that he does not prick them too deeply, because their skin is bare of flesh, and one sees the nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech which is on the rump is good as for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the leech be large, and be of iron, that she has need to well suck; and perhaps, if she were subtle, she would break; and then she makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches of the legs are applied openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soothe the flowers; and are in their place at the two shins, and the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the leech is that you put it first empty, and suck temperately, and put it on gently, and move it equally, and do not cease to do this, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then finish, and replace the leeches, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make broad wounds, and a poke deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first time to subtly open the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to make a third incision; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, let us often prick it back again; and if the vein is thin, we shall pierce it well, and the end of that is that the veins should be pierced soundly, and it behoves him who has thick skin and hard, and who have porous ears, that thou oil their places with leeches of oil appetizing and dissolving: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond oil sweet, or oil of cucumber seed; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or lilies, or chamomile, or something similar.
