Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm, or dill oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, there is no need to put any oil, but after the aeration of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, rise from ease with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should rise from old wine, or from water of the fig tree, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar; and it does not agree to bleed with a leech before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or II; and do not sleep after the leeching, and it is necessary that he should wear, when he must be leeched and when he is leeched. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are recovering are choleric, and if their body is too hot and inflamed; then it behooves them to eat cold things, such as pomegranate, endives and lettuce at the meal, and similar things; and minced pigeons, and mutton meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, let them take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and cumin seeds, and fennel seeds, and small onions and pigeons; and on the day that he will be ventosaed, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men once or twice triacle or muscade before or after ventosation, in order to comfort the main members; and let the concoction be subtle, but it is not fitting for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are put on without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the bladder and the hips and the groin, because these members do not tolerate being hurt on themselves, and one does it only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we put them on the breasts when the milk flows; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and the bladder to lessen the member; and to remove pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, since it removes by its attractive virtue possibly the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is held-back wind, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck alone so much; and sometimes are administered together with fire, and some times full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water where herbs suitable to it have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two parts of large and half palm breadth, and has on the side towards the middle a small hole, as for inserting a needle, and be of brass or iron, so that it does not burn the patient when placed upon the limb; and in the middle have a rod across of brass or iron to put a burning candle into, and let them be large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the cupping glasses of children are other than those of the elderly, and of the thin ones than of the fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And must one thus put this suction cup upon the limb: take the wick of wax or the linen, and place it in the suction cup through the rod which is inside the suction cup, so that the clarity be at the bottom of the suction cup that it not burn the patient; and then put it upon the limb, and the ears should be upon the opening that we have said, so that when one wants, there goes the vapor, and remove one the suction cup; and take the linen as before, and restart often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered in illness of pleuresin, to all acute, has no stem nor pointed, and is not administered except when it is full of liquid, and is placed upon the limb only so much; and this is the form. 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech are not used except in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in their bare flesh, such as two or three, and other similar things; and the qualities of using it is that when you find leeches which are in clear sweet water without any covering, take them; and place them in a little bit of sweet water, until they become full and have nothing in their bellies; and then leech them from the vein and cupping glass, then rub the member until it is red, and place the leeches on top; and when they are full and swell up, if it is where one can put a cupping glass, put it there because it is very good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, then lift the part of the aisil, and then with water, very well, and then the sprint; and if the parts heal too much after the body of the senses, then wet I drapel of linen in cold water, and put on, until the sinews are stretched; and if the sinews are multiplied, then put on vitriol ground, or gall, and similar things, as long as it is stretched; or you put on the part half of peeled beans, and let them until they dry out in the place, so it will stop now; and if you need more, then take other senses.  
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the tweezers do not want to take them, rub the place with fresh blood, or put a needle there until the hair comes out, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will rise; and when you see that they are falling, put some powder of aloes and silk ground, or ashes, and they will now fall. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear child, that the fool looks in this chapter, they never saw any of the old books, nor read a letter; and for this reason, science is estranged in our land, because I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the knowledge of the old books, where I studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have taught you described in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and clearly showed the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I did in these II chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say here in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprains come to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to cure the patient on one part and on the other, if nothing of the sort prevents him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his strength is not very hot, nor too cold; and avoid cold things, namely, cold meats, and flesh of lamb and kid, and drink no wine, and avoid any fatty foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meat which fills the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt of a hot abscess, or of an expansion of matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to his first government that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or they have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testae, and pies, and vetch belly, and eels, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment it regains strength and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken of the old and decrepit cannot well be taken back or joined together according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of little children; but no matter, reset the broken bone with large bandages which will hold it and join the limb together, until it forces as it was before; and do not let any point of its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish them with large meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, or of the thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the shaft and others that are sharp, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with a fracture, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner has its engine and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which its ends are twisted, and opens well by force, and feels to the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor feeling on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you must not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after, and then restrain it carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in a circle, and the two parts are disjoined, it is necessary now to put them together evenly, so that abscesses should not come; and if abscesses come, let him leave them for any day, until the abscesses are appeased; then put it equal to the measure that you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then restrain it, as it is necessary after.  
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in pieces, whether it is of two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or to the hand if it is a small member, or to two cords, or to one cord and to the hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you set by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that through your work there comes no lesion nor pain to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient feels it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well; then draw it beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come from their abscess work hot and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, carefully instruct the patient that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it is necessary to put him in such a disposition that he feels no pain; and guard yourself that it be placed straightly, so that tortuosity does not come when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and thin linen cloth; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard linen band, because the wide bands embrace the whole large limb and restrain it from all sides equally so that there is no gap; then bind around light splints, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the entire band, then go above the fracture and tighten less than the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you reach a large part of the healthy side, then take the other bandage, and turn it back directly above the broken side; then return to the part below the fracture, and tighten moderately, neither too hard nor too loose, as we have said in the first hour above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloth, so that they are all equal, then tie everything from above with a bandage, and then put your well-made poultices on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.  
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put upon it a soothing thing for the abscess, hot, and which removes the swelling, and let it remain so for some days; then place upon the swollen area a bandage of half a length cane skillfully wrapped, or of wood from which we make cloaks, or palm branches, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is necessary for the limb of small size or large; then tighten on the splints as you did in the first hour, then tie above a thread evenly, as in the first hour above the fracture; tighter it is above, less below; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want from the works of fools who make their ligatures with ropes of twisted linen thread, and this is a great error, because the ligament cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that between each splint there be less than two fingers' width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bothered by the points of the stitches after tightening them in their healthy parts, put underneath them pads of linen, or wool fleece, so that he does not become sore.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it does not befit to put splints except after V days or VII, or more according to your surety of the abscess arriving; and see here the manner of the plasters ancients for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour that is held at the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, neither too bright nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture to more dispositions, and also to women and to small children, for it is not too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three parts each of  bark, ladani,  henbane, asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mucilage, ana x; myrrh and aloes, ana v; alechil viii; and make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is good for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsion: take mugwort and viper's bugloss, ana X III; myrrh and aloes, ana IX III; acacia VI III; Armenian bole X III, and grind well, and confit with water or the yolk of an egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to bandage joints and bones that are dislocated from their places, and to soothe the pain that arises, and the usage of bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in wine and oil cooked, and put it upon the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and taking away pain properly. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth laurel leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaister for the restoration of the bone fracture and to lessen the remainder of the abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of verbena, one part each; and grind, and boil with wine, and if the limb is burned, boil it with moist coriander water, or water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of setting more forcefully than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras states in his book that one should put on the broken limb for restoration only a certain one made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one should put upon the broken member, to restore, things dry a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for the lesion and pain: take mugwort and heads of worms decocted, or feathers of ostrich, and mallow, and silk equally, and grind them up, and make a plaster of it and lay it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you loosen it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, or if the bone has moved from its place; if not, do not loosen it for several days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the splint now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea moisture, and plunge it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, half in water or in rose oil, and tie on a bandage, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then begin the fine stitching, and a little bit of splint, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and suture until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and pain and swelling are entirely gone, and you need plaster and bandage, then begin again as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb nothing of that which we have said, so do not unbind it before III days or IV or V or VII; and no time leave it XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and approaches the adjustment of the bone on top; therefore restrain it more than the first, and thickens its flesh, as I said before; and if you see it drying more than necessary is, know that nursings cannot come there; arose then from warm water tepid, all the time that you unbind it, and this be each third day, and soften a little the limb; by this work therefore shortens the nursings in the limb, and repairs quickly what do foolish mire, that returned the limb crooked: this is bad, and so is works fearful, and I see no other thing than to leave it and operate it rightly. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone all the bone up to the syfa which is under the bone, like it is made high or fast; and because of this is called this way of fracture "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or a splitting or of the collarbone of the stone, or of the head on the stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the skin that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is put back into the bone as subtle as a horsehair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound which is made or by striking with stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and it makes the piece of bone go down, and the bones are like the blacksmiths when they forge on the cauldrons; so enters the stone inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or whose chief is moist bones, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that are broken into small pieces like stars; and I will speak of it in its place.  
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by deduction on them, and the inquiry at their tendons, and by the corrupt cartilage which is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of capillary is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs it gently, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take heed to the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes becoming watery and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an impossible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the skin beneath the bone does not rot and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes to the cloth that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the split part thus: and it is that you prick the head of the patient carefully, and uncover on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more softly than you can, and if discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess applies, if he helps with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with bandages moistened in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess applies is appeased, and be assured of discharge of blood; then begin to remove the bone around, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you cut at the narrow end in front, and it is the shape: 
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of cuts of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, both pointed and of iron, and work lightly so that you do not break the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and rough, it is necessary that you pierce it first, so that you administer splints with drill bits, do not make them go beyond the bone, and should have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have more of these, so that each one comes in its place from the thickness of the bone, so that you have splints for all bones; and this is the shape of three types of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one drill bit on the bone, and turn at your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill bit elsewhere a little later, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pliers, tweezers; and keep that you do not touch the marrow nor the syfac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the appliance which is dislodged from the bone to all other instruments seeming like a chisel, but it is necessary that it be more rigid and finer than the other chisel; and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or no scales, then cure the wounds lightly with the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of treatment is that Galen says, which is drier; and praise it greatly, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the broken part appears exposed, so that when you have uncovered that portion, you will place under the head of this lens-shaped incision tool, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and is the part sharp in II coasts, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be well guarded of the cloth that is below; if it adheres to the bone, gently remove it, because one removes it easily without nuisance, and without fear.  
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the broken bone does not pierce to the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to reapply this asperity, and remove the scales with a fine razor which you must have in various quantities, to apply in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you apply care according to its requirement; and this thing is not well responded to by anyone who has placed his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, then you must take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so that you don't injure the wound, then administer a bandage above, and do not tighten it more than necessary so long as it holds the wound alone; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the pus has subsided, then undo it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and ground almond meal, and incense powder, and arnica, and similar things; and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer additional medicines that are not biting in nature; and guard so that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any oil, nor let any pus collect; because when pus collects on the surface of the brain, it rots and causes great harm to the patient; for when one puts a biting substance on the wound, it festers upwards. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take ward, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the black does not come out except for the medicine that one has put on it, which has virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil, and glue one cloth to it, and put it on the ulcer; then cure it in the manner of cures that is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the lower jaw are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your little finger or point in the middle of them, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and with the palm outwards, until the bones return according to their natural shape; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.  
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come to its place, then it behoves you to put it even at the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another band, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed, then wrap in three linen bandages at the head, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be softened in the preparation of auburn from an egg, and powdered mill; then leave the tent, as long as the bones are hard, and the cartilages hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in their place, and if a thin cloth is wrapped around it, and the wound adheres, and blows on the patient; do what you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the boil while you are working on it, put a piece of cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or one spoonful of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, apply a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, mixed with yolk of egg, then put light bandages on top, and do not bind it at all neither; and if the fracture of the bones is small, and broken into small pieces, then extract them with instruments suitable for this, then stitch the gap, and cure with things enjanrans flesh, and soldering, as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside, so it cures with tents, and put wads of wool in it, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw rupture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken apart below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outside and not broken in two, except that it splinters inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the mouth of the sick person; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your right index finger in and gently push the fracture inward, and fix it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is separated into two pieces, then it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then strain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw cerote, and place on it one double drapel; and place on the drapel a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or flaxseed flour, after which you have removed the cerote; and place a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plasters adhere, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of the bone is removed; so subtle of the remove with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then close the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable for this, to prevent flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: or it is broken and severed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken bone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each part of the fracture to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no appearance or flaw.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth or wool, and be it large according to your need; and being and lightly lifting the bone, and straining the sphere with your hand, so that you put each part of the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder with force because it comes in its way, then it is necessary that the patient lie supine on his bed, and put below the shoulder one hour glass full, and shove the ministers’ shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the fracture to your two hands, and if you find it broken, then it is necessary that you split it upwards; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any raising, then cut one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, to ward off the sifac.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And seems like a spoon, and is not too heavy, and be also as wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and have II heads, as you see, and be one wide, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of hot abscess, so sew the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, so apply the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, moisten one bandage in rose oil and honey and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you place upon the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of yolk of egg, and put light bandages above, and put a spear under the armpit, if you have need; then take a very great band of one palm wide, then put the double drape above the bandages, and the plaster; then take a strip subtle of III two of wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage be hanging; and put the strip upon the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the armpit healthy, and under the armpit wounded; and tighten each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, so reward each day, and when the ligaments slacken, so restrain it; and make the patient lie upon his back, and put him when he sleeps the small roller under the armpit, to raise the shoulder upwards; thus will lighten the fracture of the shoulder by lightening of the shoulder blade, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accident comes, until XX days; then renew the plaster, if you see that it has need, and restrain and leave it so, until it be restored; and it is restored in at most XXVIII days, and in less in some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or separates in the middle, and one feels it only by touch; therefore, set it according to the figure of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on top a double cloth.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes beforehand, and not below the heart, then do as before, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the arm to appease an abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it goes down to the bone, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and thirst, and perhaps vomits blood, and the mouth opens on the broken bone, and he feels all good. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and put .i. cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the sides of the two bones with your hands, and subtly bring them in all ways as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages over the fine layer of salt, or another light cloth, and wrap it in .i. bandage, and tie it above the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage round at the back, and restrain it firmly, and rewind every hour the strap, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, and wipe off the plaster, and address what has come there in ways of cures; then put back the plaster, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only for that cause because they are glassy; and one feels it well upon inquiry as to the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the broken piece equal.  
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint on it, and restrain it with a stick, if you have need of it. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is inclining inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and pricking, as well as from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and besides prickings, and all and vomiting great plants of blood, and it is of grief sickness, and the ancients have put great engines there.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats that inflate the belly, in order to expel the wind from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of us put suction cups on the spot in order to draw out fluids forcefully, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup does not draw the superfluities to the location for the purpose of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say any one of you must cover the place with wool moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the middle part, then be cured of the treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone which pierces the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under it an instrument to ward off the syfac; and then one must carve the bone, and drain gently, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is great, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put upon it moist cloths in rose oil, and put upon the place; and cure while the place of him as it is fitting for the abscess, and be lying on his back or upon the side where it must, until he is healed.  
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it sometimes happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, if you take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.  
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many positions, and if they move well when pulled and stopped, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given to it. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is sound or not, then take care if the legs are softened, and if the accident there is which are in hands, and on the back there is windiness and expulsion without will; and when one has supported it on its belly, then there is expulsion without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is healed on its back and he wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in its care. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, it is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward if there is an abscess hot, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a linen bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cover on the joint; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture; then cure with an ointment that promotes healing, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," put your fist of your left hand in there, and make it even with the other hand on your power, then put on the plaster and splint, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do this again, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens sometimes that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, if it had not been for a little lessening at the top; and making it long, and declining to the side, and comes to the patient pain at the place, and tingling, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand upon it, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the figure of it; and if the fracture is at the top only, then put equal the fracture, as long as it is to natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, then make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, place it on the board, then place on a splint of wood or of cork, and restrain the splints so that it does not move; and apply the bandage under the ribs until the wound is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
