And when it is equal, put a drying plaster with abundance of egg, and then the poultices, and then the stick of a tablet of III inches long, that encompasses the place of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient to fine nourishment, until he is healed; and if any thing comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stick that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of plank, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and one thinks that this is dislocations; and it is the bone that opens, so one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only as dislocations, and not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and less dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens wider the knee of the diseased person than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot double their knee to fire; and is the leg which is below swollen with hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes on the outside, is that this accident is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens in front, is that his leg is well aligned according to its accomplishment; nonetheless, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the hip is at its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this kind of dislocation is that you should examine if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, if there is no cure needed; and it is not necessary for him to have presumption [confidence].
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocations, so haste that you return the joint, and the extension inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; perhaps it will return, and has no need of other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must appear I minister strong, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or to the tie that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands under his shoulders, then tightens with a single effort upon the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to take care with its appearance. When the dislocation is in the back part, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then stretch the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the strength; then seize other assistants with his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outwards in the form: it will now return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen strip above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick limb be extended two fingers more than the other; then let it be hung by the head from a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the top of the hip, and let other ministers stand with the sick person who embrace firmly the hips, because the joint now returns easily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the rear, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has sciatica, and restrain I the linen on the bad leg properly, and on the foot also; then put II tisons, I to the head and I other to the feet, then stick I tison between the hips of the patient in-between the form; and ait plantei of wet cloth around, that it does not bleach the bad limb, then extend each minister toward him, and the mire puts equal at his hand the dislocation.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, put it on a table that is, and press it as we have said in the [previous] section, and lay the patient on his healthy side.  
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is before, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the one who has eyes his pain to be on the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and the extension downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the rear, it does not behoove to stretch the patient down, nor raise up on the ground, but rather he should be as if the hip was dislocated in the rear, like we have said about laying on the two hips; and be on his face, and the linen extended like we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table; and it will be good when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal; then adjust the hips, and put on the plaster, and the restraint of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest three days or four, then untie it, and put the plaster upon; and if you see that they are equal, strain it, like before, and leave it three days; then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he does not rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as much as he can, and place your back on his back, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and retract between your two, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it rests well at his hip lightly; and put the plaster on, and make the leg air at the hip, and bind them together firmly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not make the patient work to go, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes broken, and sometimes dislocated completely, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning is light, and one must extend it gently with his hands when it is only bruised. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from its whole, it behoves that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the ministers except by the leg, above the ankle; then draw the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with the left twice, then upward, and push the foot beautifully upward; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is well; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a stake firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie drapes around, so that it does not bleed the patient; then hold the ministers by the hip, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the ligature, so that it lies on the neck of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and let the stakes be placed between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when we are extending; then put the mire equally in the dislocation with your hands, and other ministers hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return immediately. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set, put the plaster and dressings on top, and strain it firmly, and tie his leg to the limb, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave him for II days or III, and if the bandage softens, strain it again. Then untie it after the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for IIII days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate it again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to him, then it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is fitting to extend them well without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table totally straight, and put your foot on what separates from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it comes back; and when it is equalized, and there is nothing separating, put under the sole of the foot a board at the hip, then strain firmly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and let him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at the beginning of soothing things abscess hot, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess may be warmed there; and when the limb is in its place, administer soothing things abscess hot, and cure the wound as it is proper, with dried ointments; and if with dislocation a fracture, and small bones dislocated, set the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, because this will be your death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and your body.
